Duration Requirement for Dam and Sadaqah in Ihram Violations
Dispute on the duration required for dam vs. sadaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the duration thresholds for dam and sadaqah concerning wearing sewn clothes or covering the head during ihram, and explain the Hanafi evidence and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
A complete day or night of wearing sewn clothes during ihram requires dam; less requires sadaqah — duration matters.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter of Hajj: the atonement for wearing sewn garments or covering the head while in ihram. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a full day (or night) and a shorter period. We will explore the textual basis, the first and final opinions of Imam Abu Hanifa, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prohibition
Recognize that wearing sewn clothes or covering the head during ihram is a prohibited act that requires atonement (dam or sadaqah).
2
Understand the matn ruling
The core rule: a complete day equals dam; less than a day equals sadaqah.
The matn uses 'yawman kamilan' (a complete day).
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa first agreed with Abu Yusuf that more than half a day triggers dam, then retracted and required a full day. Abu Yusuf maintained his view.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's final opinion.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The intended benefit (comfort) from wearing clothes is durational. A day is the customary measure for wearing and removing clothes. Qur'anic reference: 'sarabil taqikum al-harr' (garments protecting from heat) implies prolonged use.
Hanafi istidlal combines Qur'an and custom.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
Shafi'i argues benefit is immediate, so dam is due instantly. Hanafi responds that comfort is not complete in a moment. The practical difference: for short durations, Shafi'i requires dam, Hanafi requires sadaqah.
See thamarah al-khilaf.

وَانُ لَبسَ ثَوْبًا مُخِيْطًا أَوْ غَطَّى رَأْسَهُ يَوْمًا كَامِلا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَ مِنْ ذلِك فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا لَبِسَ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ نِصْفِ يَوْمٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَوَّلًا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجِبُ الدَّمُ بِنَفْسِ اللَّبْسِ لأَنَّ الإرتفاق يتكامل بالاشْتِمَالِ عَلى بَدَنِهِ وَلَنا أَنَّ مَعْنى التَّرْفَقِ مَقْصُودٌ مِنَ اللَّبْسِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِ الْمُدَّةِ لِيَتَحَصَّلَ عَلَى الكَمَال وَيَجبُ الدَّمُ فَقُدَرَ بِالْيَوْم لأنه يلبس فِيهِ ثُمَّ ينزع عادةً و تَتَقَاصَرُ فِيمَا دُونَهُ الْجَنايَةُ فَتَجبُ الصَّدَقَةُ غَيْرَ أنَّ أبَايُوسُفَ أقام الأكثَرَ مَقَامَ الكُل
ترجمہ اور اگر محرم نے سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنایا اپنا سر ڈھکا پورے ایک دن تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور اگر اس سے کم ہے تو اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف" سے مروی ہے کہ جب اس نے نصف یوم سے زیادہ پہنا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور یہی ابو حنیفہ کا پہلا قول ہے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ پہنتے ہی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ راحت کا نفع اٹھانا اس کے بدن پر شامل ہوتے ہی کامل ہو جائے گا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ پہننے سے راحت کے معنی مقصود ہیں تو ایک مدت کا اعتبار ضروری ہے تا کہ راحت مقصود علی سبیل الکمال حاصل ہو اور دم واجب ہو ۔ پس وہ مدت ایک یوم مقرر کی گئی ہے کیونکہ عادہ دن میں لباس پہنا جاتا پھر اتار دیا جاتا ہے اور ایک دن سے کم میں جنایت قاصر ہے اس لئے صدقہ واجب ہوگا مگر ابو یوسف نے اکثر کو کل کے قائم مقام کیا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم نے سلا ہوا کپڑا ایک دن یا ایک رات پہنایا اپنا سر ایک دن یا ایک رات ڈھکے رہا تو اس پر دم واجب ہوگا اور اگر ایک دن یا ایک رات سے کم میں یہ مل پایا گیا تو صدقہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول اول بھی یہی ہے پھر اس سے رجوع فرما کر کہنے لگے تھے کہ دم اسی وقت واجب ہو گا جبکہ پورے ایک دن یا ایک رات پہنا ہو۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنتے ہی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ راحت کا انتفاع حاصل کرنا کپڑا پہنتے ہیں مکمل ہو جاتا ہے پس جب کپڑا پہنتے ہی نفع راحت کامل ہو جاتا ہے، جرم کامل پایا گیا تو اس پر بالیقین دم واجب ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کپڑا پہننے سے راحت کے معنی مقصود ہیں یعنی گرمی سردی دور کرنا کیونکہ پہنا اسی واسطے ہے۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے سَرَابِيلَ تَقِيْكُمُ الْحَرَّ اور یہ عنی دراز ہوتے ہیں لہذا یہ معنی کامل بھی ہوگا اور قاصر بھی ہوگا اور کامل و قاصر کے درمیان حد فاصل ضروری ہے تا کہ جزا ، اسی کے مطابق متعین کی جائے ۔ پس حد فاصل ایک دن یا ایک رات کو قرار دیا گیا یعنی ایک دن کامل یا ایک رات کامل پہننا کامل جرم ہے اس کی وجہ سے جزاء کامل یعنی دم واجب ہو گا اور اس سے کم جرم قاصر ہے لہذا اس کی وجہ سے جزاء قاصر یعنی صدقہ واجب ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف چونکہ اکثر کو کل کے قائم مقام رکھتے ہیں اس لئے ان کے نزدیک اکثر یوم میں پہننے کی صورت میں بھی جزاء کامل یعنی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔
If he wears a sewn garment or covers his head for a complete day, then dam is binding upon him, and if less than that, then sadaqah. How much of a day is considered 'most'? The sayings of the jurists: 'And if he wore a sewn garment or covered his head for a complete day, then upon him is dam, and if it is less than that, then upon him is sadaqah. And from Abu Yusuf that if he wore more than half a day, then upon him is dam, and this was the first saying of Abu Hanifa. And al-Shafi'i said: dam becomes wajib by the very act of wearing, because the benefit is completed by encompassing his body. And our proof is that the meaning of comfort is intended from wearing, so a duration must be considered to achieve completeness, and dam becomes wajib. So it was estimated by a day because it is worn during the day then removed as a custom, and the violation is deficient in less than that, so sadaqah becomes wajib. However, Abu Yusuf considered the majority as standing in place of the whole.' Translation: And if the muhrim wore a sewn garment or covered his head for a full day, then dam is wajib upon him, and if less than that, then sadaqah is wajib. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that when he wore more than half a day, then dam is wajib, and this was Abu Hanifa's first saying. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: dam becomes wajib by the very act of wearing, because the benefit of comfort is completed by covering his body. And our proof is that the meaning of comfort is intended from wearing, so a duration must be considered to achieve the desired comfort in a complete manner, and dam becomes wajib. So that duration was set as one day because customarily clothing is worn during the day then removed, and in less than that the violation is deficient, so sadaqah is wajib. However, Abu Yusuf considered the majority as standing in place of the whole. Explanation of the matter: The case is that if the muhrim wore a sewn garment for a day or a night, or covered his head for a day or a night, then dam is wajib. And if less than a day or a night, then sadaqah is wajib. And Imam Abu Hanifa's first saying was also this; then he retracted and said that dam is only wajib when he wore a complete day or night. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: dam becomes wajib immediately upon wearing the sewn garment. His proof is that obtaining the benefit of comfort is completed right when the garment is worn; so when the benefit is complete, a complete crime is found, so definitively dam is wajib. Our proof is that the meaning of comfort from wearing a garment is intended, i.e., to repel heat and cold, because that is why it is worn. Thus Allah's saying: 'Garments that protect you from heat' and these meanings may be prolonged, so these meanings can be complete or deficient. A dividing line is needed between complete and deficient to determine the recompense accordingly. So the dividing line was set as one day or one night: wearing a full day or full night is a complete crime, incurring complete recompense (dam), and less than that is a deficient crime, incurring deficient recompense (sadaqah). And because Abu Yusuf considers the majority as standing in place of the whole, according to him, wearing for most of the day also incurs complete recompense (dam).
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a muhrim wearing a sewn garment (mukhayyat) or covering his head. It is a ruling_with_proof, containing an intra-Hanafi dispute and a response to Imam al-Shafi'i. The matn states: if a muhrim wears a sewn garment or covers his head for a complete day (yawm kamil), he owes dam; if less, he owes sadaqah. Abu Yusuf transmits (and it was Abu Hanifa's first opinion) that wearing more than half a day counts as a full day, thus incurring dam. Al-Shafi'i holds that dam is due immediately upon wearing, because the benefit is instantaneous. The Hanafi response (li-anna) argues that the intended benefit is the comfort of covering the body, which is not fully realized until a sufficient duration passes. The day was chosen as the measure because it is the customary period for wearing and removing clothing. For less than a day, the violation is deficient (qasirah), so sadaqah suffices. However, Abu Yusuf's principle of considering the majority as equivalent to the whole (al-akthar yuqamu maqam al-kull) leads him to require dam for more than half a day. The commentary (sharh) clarifies: a full day or night triggers dam; less than that triggers sadaqah. Abu Hanifa later retracted his first opinion and adopted the full-day requirement. The disagreement with Shafi'i is based on the nature of the crime: immediate vs. durational.

Key Terms
یوم کامل (yawm kamil): A complete day (24 hours) or a complete night (12 hours). The matn says 'yawman kamilan' which is a full day. Commentary clarifies that a full night is equivalent.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Here, half a sa' of wheat or its value as atonement for a deficient violation (less than a full day/night).
مخيط (mukhayyat): Sewn garment made to fit the body (like shirts, pants).
دم (dam): Slaughter of a sheep (or equivalent) as atonement for a complete violation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, what atonement is required if a muhrim wears a sewn garment for a full night (12 hours)?
A) Dam, because a full night is equivalent to a full day.
B) Sadaqah, because it is less than 24 hours.
C) No atonement, because night is not considered.
D) Qada, because the ihram is invalidated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a full day or night of wearing sewn clothes or covering the head to incur dam; less requires sadaqah.

Kaffarah for Using Perfumed Substances in Ihram: The Distinction of Essence
States kaffarah rules for perfumed substances used as medicine vs. perfume

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah for a muhrim using musk as medicine versus as perfume, and identify the decisive factor (essence vs. intent).

Core Idea
For inherently perfumed substances like musk, all use triggers kaffarah; for ordinary substances, only use as perfume does.

In ihram, using perfume is prohibited and incurs kaffarah, but using medicine generally does not. However, for substances that are perfumes in essence—like musk, amber, and camphor—even medicinal use demands compensation. This passage clarifies that the decisive factor is the substance's essence, not the user's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of substances
The ruling distinguishes between substances that are not inherently perfumed (e.g., lightly scented oils) and those that are inherently perfumed (musk, amber, camphor). Recognize which category each substance falls into.
2
Determine the condition for kaffarah for general substances
For non-inherent perfumes, kaffarah is wajib only if they are used as perfume (intent of beautification). If used as medicine, no kaffarah.
Intent is the key factor here.
3
Analyze the ruling for inherently perfumed substances
For musk, amber, camphor, kaffarah is wajib even when used as medicine. The prohibition attaches to the substance itself, so the condition of using as perfume is not required.
Essence overrides intent.
4
Apply the rule to a new example
Test with rosewater: is it inherently perfumed? If yes, then even medicinal use requires kaffarah. If not, then only use as perfume triggers kaffarah.
Practice classifying substances.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i may differentiate based on intent for all substances. Understand that this Hanafi position is more stringent for inherently perfumed items.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استعمال بطور خوشبو کے کیا گیا ہے تب تو کفارہ یعنی دم یا صدقہ واجب ہوگا اور اگر بطور علاج استعمال کیا گی تو اس پر کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر مشک یا عنبر یا کافور وغیرہ کا استعمال بطور دوا کیا تب بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ یہ چیزیں عین خوشبو میں ان میں کفارہ واجب ہونے کے لئے بطور خوشبو استعمال کرنے کی شرط نہیں ہے۔
If it is used as perfume, then kaffarah (dam or sadaqah) is obligatory. And if used as medicine, then no kaffarah is obligatory. And if musk, amber, camphor, etc., are used as medicine, even then kaffarah is obligatory because these substances are perfumes in essence; for kaffarah to be obligatory, the condition of using them as perfume is not required.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This is a ruling statement regarding the obligation of kaffarah (compensation) for a Muhrim using perfumed substances. The general rule: if an item is not inherently a perfume (e.g., medicinal oils scented lightly), using it as medicine does not incur kaffarah, while using it as perfume does. However, for substances that are perfumes in essence (like musk, amber, camphor), the ruling is stricter: any use—whether as perfume or medicine—requires kaffarah, because the prohibition is on the substance itself, not the intent. This distinction is specific to the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
کفارہ (kaffarah): Compensation for violating Ihram prohibitions, either dam (sacrifice of an animal) or sadaqah (charity).
دم (dam): Sacrifice of a sheep/goat as kaffarah.
عین خوشبو (ayn khushbu): The essence of perfume; an inherently perfumed substance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muhrim uses musk as a medicinal ointment for a wound. Is kaffarah obligatory?
A) No, because it is used as medicine.
B) Yes, because musk is inherently a perfume.
C) Only if the amount exceeds a certain limit.
D) It depends on the school; according to Imam Shafi'i, no kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
For inherently perfumed substances like musk, the Hanafi school requires kaffarah regardless of the user's intent; for other substances, intent determines the ruling.

Duration of Wearing Stitched Clothes or Covering Head in Ihram
Inter-madhhab and intra-madhhab dispute on duration threshold for Ihram violations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi duration-based ruling for Ihram violations and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A full day of wearing stitched clothes or covering the head triggers dam; less requires sadaqah—duration determines the penalty's severity.

This lesson examines a key dispute in Hajj rulings: when does a Muhrim incur dam for wearing stitched clothes or covering the head? The Hanafi school bases the ruling on a duration threshold, while the Shafi'i school sees it as immediate upon wearing. We also see an intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa's final view and Abu Yusuf's. Understanding the reasoning (talil) behind each position strengthens your grasp of legal methodology.

Guided Path
1
State the base Hanafi ruling
Identify the act (wearing stitched clothes or covering head) and the ruling: dam for a full day, sadaqah for less. Note that this is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
Full day includes a full night; the text mentions either.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf (and Abu Hanifa initially) held that more than half a day counts as a full day for dam. Abu Hanifa later retracted, requiring a full day. Understand the difference in the principle: Abu Yusuf's 'majority as the whole' vs. Abu Hanifa's strict threshold.
3
Examine the Shafi'i position and proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that dam is obligatory immediately upon wearing because the benefit of comfort is complete as soon as the garment covers the body. No duration is needed.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the purpose of wearing clothes is comfort, which can be partial or complete. A complete violation requires a complete duration of benefit, set by custom as a full day. A shorter period is a lesser crime, warranting sadaqah. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Nahl 16:81) about garments protecting from heat is cited as supporting the purpose.
The Hanafi reasoning relies on talil (rationale) and custom (urf).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a Muhrim wears a stitched shirt for one hour, Hanafi requires sadaqah; Shafi'i requires dam. This affects the pilgrim's financial obligation.

Source Text

وَانُ لَبسَ ثَوْبًا مُخِيْطًا أَوْ غَطَّى رَأْسَهُ يَوْمًا كَامِلا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَ مِنْ ذلِك فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا لَبِسَ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ نِصْفِ يَوْمٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَوَّلًا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجِبُ الدَّمُ بِنَفْسِ اللَّبْسِ لأَنَّ الإرتفاق يتكامل بالاشْتِمَالِ عَلى بَدَنِهِ وَلَنا أَنَّ مَعْنى التَّرْفَقِ مَقْصُودٌ مِنَ اللَّبْسِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِ الْمُدَّةِ لِيَتَحَصَّلَ عَلَى الكَمَال وَيَجبُ الدَّمُ فَقُدَرَ بِالْيَوْم لأنه يلبس فِيهِ ثُمَّ ينزع عادةً و تَتَقَاصَرُ فِيمَا دُونَهُ الْجَنايَةُ فَتَجبُ الصَّدَقَةُ غَيْرَ أنْ أبَايُوسُفَ أقام الأكثَرَ مَقَامَ الكُل
ترجمہ اور اگر محرم نے سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنایا اپنا سر ڈھکا پورے ایک دن تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور اگر اس سے کم ہے تو اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف" سے مروی ہے کہ جب اس نے نصف یوم سے زیادہ پہنا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اور یہی ابو حنیفہ کا پہلا قول ہے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ پہنتے ہی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ راحت کا نفع اٹھانا اس کے بدن پر شامل ہوتے ہی کامل ہو جائے گا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ پہننے سے راحت کے معنی مقصود ہیں تو ایک مدت کا اعتبار ضروری ہے تا کہ راحت مقصود علی سبیل الکمال حاصل ہو اور دم واجب ہو ۔ پس وہ مدت ایک یوم مقرر کی گئی ہے کیونکہ عادہ دن میں لباس پہنا جاتا پھر اتار دیا جاتا ہے اور ایک دن سے کم میں جنایت قاصر ہے اس لئے صدقہ واجب ہوگا مگر ابو یوسف نے اکثر کو کل کے قائم مقام کیا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم نے سلا ہوا کپڑا ایک دن یا ایک رات پہنایا اپنا سر ایک دن یا ایک رات ڈھکے رہا تو اس پر دم واجب ہوگا اور اگر ایک دن یا ایک رات سے کم میں یہ مل پایا گیا تو صدقہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول اول بھی یہی ہے پھر اس سے رجوع فرما کر کہنے لگے تھے کہ دم اسی وقت واجب ہو گا جبکہ پورے ایک دن یا ایک رات پہنا ہو۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنتے ہی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ راحت کا انتفاع حاصل کرنا کپڑا پہنتے ہیں مکمل ہو جاتا ہے پس جب کپڑا پہنتے ہی نفع راحت کامل ہو جاتا ہے، جرم کامل پایا گیا تو اس پر بالیقین دم واجب ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کپڑا پہننے سے راحت کے معنی مقصود ہیں یعنی گرمی سردی دور کرنا کیونکہ پہنا اسی واسطے ہے۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے سَرَابِيلَ تَقِيْكُمُ الْحَرَّ اور یہ عنی دراز ہوتے ہیں لہذا یہ معنی کامل بھی ہوگا اور قاصر بھی ہوگا اور کامل و قاصر کے درمیان حد فاصل ضروری ہے تا کہ جزا ، اسی کے مطابق متعین کی جائے ۔ پس حد فاصل ایک دن یا ایک رات کو قرار دیا گیا یعنی ایک دن کامل یا ایک رات کامل پہننا کامل جرم ہے اس کی وجہ سے جزاء کامل یعنی دم واجب ہو گا اور اس سے کم جرم قاصر ہے لہذا اس کی وجہ سے جزاء قاصر یعنی صدقہ واجب ہوگا اور امام ابو یوسف چونکہ اکثر کو کل کے قائم مقام رکھتے ہیں اس لئے ان کے نزدیک اکثر یوم میں پہننے کی صورت میں بھی جزاء کامل یعنی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔
And if he wears a stitched garment or covers his head for a complete day, then upon him is a dam. And if it is less than that, then upon him is sadaqah. And from Abu Yusuf: that if he wears more than half a day, then upon him is a dam, and this was Abu Hanifa's first opinion. And al-Shafi'i said: the dam becomes obligatory by the very act of wearing, because the benefit is perfected by it covering his body. And our proof: that the meaning of comfort is intended from wearing, so it is necessary to consider duration to obtain perfection, and the dam is obligatory, so it is measured by the day because one normally wears and then removes within it, and the violation is lesser for less than that, so sadaqah is obligatory. However, Abu Yusuf placed the majority in the position of the whole. Translation: And if a Muhrim wears a stitched garment or covers his head for a complete day, then dam is obligatory. And if less than that, then sadaqah is obligatory. And from Abu Yusuf: when he wears more than half a day, then dam is obligatory, and this was Abu Hanifa's first opinion. And Imam Shafi'i said: the dam becomes obligatory by the very act of wearing, because the benefit is perfected by it covering his body. And our proof: that the meaning of comfort is intended from wearing, so a duration must be considered to obtain the desired comfort fully, and dam is obligatory. So that duration is set as one day, because customarily clothes are worn during the day and then removed. And for less than a day, the violation is lesser, so sadaqah is obligatory. However, Abu Yusuf counted the majority as the whole. Commentary: The scenario is that if a Muhrim wears a stitched garment for a day or a night, or covers his head for a day or a night, then dam is obligatory. And if less than a day or night, then sadaqah is obligatory. This was also Imam Abu Hanifa's first opinion; then he retracted and said dam is only obligatory when worn for a full day or night. Imam Shafi'i said dam becomes obligatory by the very act of wearing. His proof: the benefit of comfort is complete when the garment covers the body. So when comfort is achieved, a complete violation occurs, thus dam is certain. Our proof: the meaning of comfort from wearing is intended—to ward off heat and cold—and this meaning can be complete or deficient. A boundary is needed between complete and deficient to determine the penalty. So a full day or night is set as the boundary: wearing for a full day or night is a complete violation warranting complete penalty (dam), and less is a deficient violation warranting deficient penalty (sadaqah). Since Abu Yusuf places the majority in the position of the whole, in his view wearing for most of the day warrants complete penalty (dam).
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab and intra-madhhab dispute regarding the time threshold for kaffarah when a Muhrim wears stitched clothing or covers the head. The base ruling: if the violation lasts a full day (day or night), dam is required; if less, sadaqah. Abu Hanifa initially agreed with Abu Yusuf that more than half a day counts as a full day, but then retracted to require a full day. Imam Shafi'i holds that the violation is complete at the moment of wearing, so dam is immediate. The Hanafi proof is based on the purpose of wearing clothes (comfort), which can be partial or complete; a complete day is the customary period, so a shorter period is a lesser crime deserving a lesser penalty. Abu Yusuf's position uses the principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole. The passage includes the dalil of the Quranic verse about garments protecting from heat, indicating the purpose. This is a clear expansion of the matn by the commentator, incorporating differences and reasons.

Key Terms
دم (dam): Sacrifice of a sheep as kaffarah for a major Ihram violation.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Charity given as kaffarah for minor violations; here it refers to giving a specific amount (e.g., half a sa' of wheat) or equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final Hanafi position, if a Muhrim covers his head for half a day, what kaffarah is required?
A) Dam
B) Sadaqah
C) Nothing
D) It depends on the school

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets a full day as the threshold for dam in Ihram clothing violations; lesser durations require only sadaqah.

Non-Standard Wearing of Stitched Clothes in Ihram
Ruling on non-standard stitched garment usage in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that wearing stitched clothes in an unconventional manner does not incur a penalty, and explain the role of custom (urf) in determining the prohibition.

Core Idea
Wearing a stitched garment unconventionally is not a violation because the prohibition targets customary usage.

The prohibition on stitched clothing in ihram is not absolute—it depends on how the garment is worn. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies that if a muhrim uses a qamis or trousers in a manner that is not the customary way of wearing stitched clothes, no penalty applies. The ruling is based on the concept that the violation is defined by the common practice of wearing such garments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts described
The passage describes using a qamis as a cloak (irtidā'), wrapping with it (ittishāḥ), or making an izār from trousers. Also inserting shoulders into a cloak without inserting arms.
These are all non-standard uses.
2
Recognize the basis for no penalty
The text states that the muhrim did not wear the garment in the manner of stitched clothing (lam yalbas-hu labsa al-makhīṭ). The prohibition is tied to the specific way a garment is normally worn.
Custom (urf) defines what constitutes 'wearing' for the prohibition.
3
Consider the objection of Imam Zufar
Zufar argues that any insertion of body parts into a stitched garment triggers the penalty. The Hanafi response is that the customary manner is to insert both shoulders and arms; partial insertion does not count as proper wearing.
This highlights the Hanafi reliance on urf.
4
Draw the ruling
Since the garment is not worn in the usual way, no penalty (dam or sadaqah) is obligatory. The act is permissible (mubah) in terms of penalty, though the garment is still stitched.

وَ لَوِ ارْتَدَى بِالْقَمِيصِ أو اتَّشَحَ بِه أو اتَّزَرَ بِالسَّرَاوِيلِ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَلْبَسُهُ لبَسَ الْمَخِيطِ وَكَذَا لَو ادخل ادْخَلَ منكِبَيْهِ فِى الْقَبَاءِ وَلَمْ يَدْخُلُ يَدَيْهِ فِي الْكُمَيْنِ خِلَاقًا لرفُرَ لِأَنَّهُ مَالَيسَهُ لُبْسَ الْقَبَاءِ وَلِهَذَا يَتَكَلَّفُ فِى حِفْظه وَ التَّقْدِيرُ فِي تَعْطِيةِ الرَّأْسِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْوَقْتِ مَا بَيْنَاهُ وَلَا خِلَافَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا غَطَى جَمِيعَ رَأْسِهِ يَوْمًا كَا مِلا يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ الدَّمُ لأنَّهُ مَمْنُوعٌ عَنْهُ وَلَوْ غَطَّى بَعْضَ رَأْسِهِ فَالْمَرْوِيُّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ أَنَّهُ اعْتَبَرَ الرّبعَ إِعْتِبَارًا بِالْحَلْقِ وَالْعَوْرَةِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ سَتْرَ الْبَعْضِ اسْتِمْتَاعٌ مَقْصُودٌ يُعْتَادُهُ بَعْضُ النَّاسِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ الَّهُ يَعْتَبِرُ وأكْثَرَ الرَّأْسِ اِعْتِبَارًا للحقيقة
ترجمہ اور اگر محرم نے قمیص کو بطور چادر اوڑھا یا قمیص سے انتشاح کیا یا پانجامہ کے ساتھ لنگی باندھی تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے سلے ہوئے کپڑے کو پہننے کے طور پر نہیں پہنا اور اسی طرح اگر قباء میں اپنے مونڈھے ڈالے اور آستینوں میں اپنے دونوں ہاتھ نہیں ڈالے۔ برخلاف امام زفر کے قول کے کیونکہ اس نے قبا پہننے کے طور پر اس کو نہیں پہنا اور اسی وجہ سے وہ اس کی حفاظت میں تکلف کرے گا۔ اور سر ڈھکنے کے حق میں باعتبار وقت کے وہی اندازہ ہے جو ہم نے بیان کر دیا۔ اور اس بارے میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں جبکہ اس نے اپنے سر کو پورے ایک دن ڈھکا تو اس پر قربانی واجب ہوگی کیونکہ یہ امرممنوع ہے اور اگر اس نے تھوڑا سر ڈھکا تو ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ چوتھائی کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا حلق اور عورت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور یہ اس لئے کہ بعض کا ستر انتفاع مقصود ہے یہ بعض لوگوں کی عادت ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ وہ سر کے اکثر کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں حقیقت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے۔
تشریح ارتشاح یہ ہے کہ آدمی اپنے کپڑے کو اپنے دائیں ہاتھ کے نیچے سے داخل کر کے بائیں مونڈھے پر ڈالے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم نے قمیص کو چادر کے طور پر اور ھایا اس کو دائیں بغل سے نکال کر بائیں مونڈھے پر ڈال لیا یا اسنے پائجامہ کولنگی بنالیا یعنی لنگی کی طرح اسکو ٹانگوں میں لپیٹ لیا تو ان صورتوں میں اس صدقہ وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے اس طرح نہیں پہنا جس طرح سلے ہوئے کپڑے کو پہنا جاتا ہے اور جب سلے ہوئے کپڑے کی طرح نہیں پہنا تو اس پر دم جنایت بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک اس پر جزاء واجب ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قباء سلا ہوا لباس ہے پس جب محرم نے اسمیں اپنے مونڈھوں کو داخل کیا تو وہ سلے ہوئے کپڑے کو پہنے والا ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ قباء اسی طرح پہنی جاتی ہے اور جب محرم نے سلا ہوا کپڑا پہن لیا تو اس پر بالیقین جزاء جنایت واجب ہوگی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اسنے قباء اس طرح نہیں پہنی جس طرح اس کو پہننے کی عادت ہے۔ قباء کو عادتا پہنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں مونڈھے اور دونوں ہاتھ اس میں داخل کر دیے جائیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ہاتھوں کو آستینوں میں داخل نہ کرنے کی صورت میں قباء کی فاظت میں تکلف کرے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں اس کا کندھے پر ٹھہر نا مشکل ہے پس جب قباء کو پہننے کے طور پر نہیں پہنا گیا تو اس پر دو جنایت وغیر و جزا بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ وجزاء صاحب بدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سر ڈھانکنے میں بھی کامل ایک یوم کا اعتبار ہے چنانچہ اگر محرم نے پورے ایک دن اپنے سر کو ڈھانکا تو
Wearing a qamis as a cloak, or making iḑtibā‘ with it, or making an izār (loincloth) from a pajama — nothing becomes obligatory. And if he drapes the qamis over his shoulders (irtidā’), or wraps himself with it (ittishāḥ), or makes an izār from a sirwāl (trousers), then there is no harm, because he did not wear it as stitched clothing is worn. Similarly, if he inserts his shoulders into a qabā’ (cloak) but does not insert his hands into the sleeves, contrary to the view of Zufar, because he did not wear it as a qabā’ is worn, and for this reason he would have difficulty keeping it on. And the estimation for covering the head in terms of time is as we have explained. And there is no difference that if he covers all of his head for a complete day, dam is obligatory upon him because it is prohibited. And if he covers part of his head, then it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he considered the quarter, by analogy with shaving and the ‘awrah. This is because covering part is a sought-after benefit and is customary for some people. And from Abu Yusuf that he considers the majority of the head, by considering the reality. Translation: And if a Muhrim wears a qamis as a cloak, or makes itishah with the qamis, or ties a lungi (wrap) with a pajama, then there is no harm, because he did not wear the stitched garment in the manner of wearing stitched clothing. And similarly, if he puts his shoulders into a qabā’ but does not put his hands into the sleeves, contrary to Imam Zufar’s view, because he did not wear it as a qabā’ is worn, and for this reason he would have difficulty keeping it on. And regarding covering the head, the estimation of time is as we have stated. And there is no difference that if he covers all of his head for a complete day, then sacrifice (dam) is obligatory, because it is prohibited. And if he covers part of his head, then from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that he considers the quarter, by analogy with shaving and the ‘awrah. And this because covering part is a sought-after benefit that is customary for some people. And from Abu Yusuf that he considers the majority of the head, by considering the reality. Commentary: Ittishāḥ is that a man puts his garment under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder. The scenario: If a Muhrim uses a qamis as a cloak, or takes it from under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder, or makes a lungi from a pajama (i.e., wraps it around his legs like a loincloth), then in these cases no sadaqah etc. becomes obligatory, because he did not wear it in the manner stitched clothing is worn. And when he does not wear it like stitched clothing, then the penalty for violation is not obligatory. And according to Imam Zufar, penalty is obligatory. His proof: the qabā’ is stitched clothing, so when the Muhrim inserts his shoulders into it, he becomes a wearer of stitched clothing, because qabā’ is worn like that, and when he wears stitched clothing, penalty is certain. Our proof: he did not wear the qabā’ in the customary manner. The customary way of wearing a qabā’ is to insert both shoulders and both hands. For this reason, if he does not put his hands in the sleeves, he will have difficulty keeping it on, because it is hard to keep it on the shoulders. So when it is not worn as a qabā’ is worn, no penalty is obligatory. And the author of Bada’i‘ says that for covering the head, a full day is to be considered. So if a Muhrim covers all his head for a full day, then...
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct sub-rulings. First: wearing stitched clothing in an unconventional manner (e.g., using a qamis as a wrapper, or wearing a cloak without inserting arms) does not incur the prohibition penalty, because the violation is defined by the customary method of wearing. Imam Zufar dissents, arguing that any insertion of body parts into stitched clothing triggers the penalty, but the Hanafi position relies on the custom (urf) of how such garments are normally worn. Second: covering the head partially. There is consensus that covering the entire head for a full day requires dam. For partial covering, Abu Hanifa uses qiyas on shaving the head (where covering a quarter is considered significant) and on the exposure of the ‘awrah (where covering a quarter triggers obligation); he sets the threshold at one quarter of the head. Abu Yusuf looks to the reality of covering and considers the majority of the head as the threshold. The commentary also clarifies that for the time aspect, the earlier ruling (full day) applies. Note that the last sentence is incomplete at the page break.

Key Terms
اضطباع (iḍṭibā‘): To wear a garment by passing it under the right armpit and throwing it over the left shoulder.
انتشاح (ittishāḥ): To envelope oneself with a garment, specifically by wrapping it around the body.
لبس المخيط (labs al-makhīṭ): Wearing stitched clothing in the customary manner (e.g., arms through sleeves).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muhrim wears a stitched coat by putting only his left arm in one sleeve and leaving the right arm out. The coat is secured only by the left sleeve. According to the Hanafi school, does this incur a penalty?
A) Yes, because his left arm is inserted into a stitched sleeve.
B) No, because the coat is not worn on both shoulders and arms in the customary manner.
C) Yes, because the coat is stitched and covers part of his body.
D) Only if he wears it for more than half a day.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of stitched clothing in ihram is defined by customary wearing; unconventional use does not incur a penalty.

Partial Head Covering in Ihram: Thresholds and Qiyas
Ruling on partial head covering in ihram with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on partial head covering in ihram, distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the threshold, and explain the qiyas used.

Core Idea
Covering a quarter of the head triggers the same penalty as shaving, based on qiyas; the full day requirement for full coverage is agreed.

Covering the head in ihram is prohibited, but what if only part is covered? This passage addresses the threshold that triggers a penalty. It also establishes that covering the entire head for a complete day necessitates dam (sacrifice), and then presents the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on partial coverage, with Abu Hanifa using qiyas to shaving and ‘awrah to set the threshold at one quarter, while Abu Yusuf considers the majority of the head.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
There is consensus that covering all of the head for a full day obligates dam.
Time is also a factor: the earlier ruling that a full day triggers penalty is referenced.
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf on partial coverage
For partial covering, Abu Hanifa sets the threshold at a quarter of the head, while Abu Yusuf sets it at the majority.
The difference stems from their methods of reasoning.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's qiyas
Abu Hanifa analogizes partial covering to shaving (halq) and to covering the ‘awrah. In both cases, covering a quarter is considered significant. Therefore, covering a quarter of the head triggers the same ruling as shaving a quarter (dam).
The illa is the quarter as the minimum significant amount.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf considers the reality of covering: covering most of the head is akin to covering the whole, so the majority is the threshold.
He relies on the concept of majority (akthar) being equivalent to the whole in rulings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's quarter threshold, as it is the main narration in the text.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Wearing a qamis as a cloak, or making iḑtibā‘ with it, or making an izār (loincloth) from a pajama — nothing becomes obligatory. And if he drapes the qamis over his shoulders (irtidā’), or wraps himself with it (ittishāḥ), or makes an izār from a sirwāl (trousers), then there is no harm, because he did not wear it as stitched clothing is worn. Similarly, if he inserts his shoulders into a qabā’ (cloak) but does not insert his hands into the sleeves, contrary to the view of Zufar, because he did not wear it as a qabā’ is worn, and for this reason he would have difficulty keeping it on. And the estimation for covering the head in terms of time is as we have explained. And there is no difference that if he covers all of his head for a complete day, dam is obligatory upon him because it is prohibited. And if he covers part of his head, then it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he considered the quarter, by analogy with shaving and the ‘awrah. This is because covering part is a sought-after benefit and is customary for some people. And from Abu Yusuf that he considers the majority of the head, by considering the reality. Translation: And if a Muhrim wears a qamis as a cloak, or makes itishah with the qamis, or ties a lungi (wrap) with a pajama, then there is no harm, because he did not wear the stitched garment in the manner of wearing stitched clothing. And similarly, if he puts his shoulders into a qabā’ but does not put his hands into the sleeves, contrary to Imam Zufar’s view, because he did not wear it as a qabā’ is worn, and for this reason he would have difficulty keeping it on. And regarding covering the head, the estimation of time is as we have stated. And there is no difference that if he covers all of his head for a complete day, then sacrifice (dam) is obligatory, because it is prohibited. And if he covers part of his head, then from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that he considers the quarter, by analogy with shaving and the ‘awrah. And this because covering part is a sought-after benefit that is customary for some people. And from Abu Yusuf that he considers the majority of the head, by considering the reality. Commentary: Ittishāḥ is that a man puts his garment under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder. The scenario: If a Muhrim uses a qamis as a cloak, or takes it from under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder, or makes a lungi from a pajama (i.e., wraps it around his legs like a loincloth), then in these cases no sadaqah etc. becomes obligatory, because he did not wear it in the manner stitched clothing is worn. And when he does not wear it like stitched clothing, then the penalty for violation is not obligatory. And according to Imam Zufar, penalty is obligatory. His proof: the qabā’ is stitched clothing, so when the Muhrim inserts his shoulders into it, he becomes a wearer of stitched clothing, because qabā’ is worn like that, and when he wears stitched clothing, penalty is certain. Our proof: he did not wear the qabā’ in the customary manner. The customary way of wearing a qabā’ is to insert both shoulders and both hands. For this reason, if he does not put his hands in the sleeves, he will have difficulty keeping it on, because it is hard to keep it on the shoulders. So when it is not worn as a qabā’ is worn, no penalty is obligatory. And the author of Bada’i‘ says that for covering the head, a full day is to be considered. So if a Muhrim covers all his head for a full day, then...

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct sub-rulings. First: wearing stitched clothing in an unconventional manner (e.g., using a qamis as a wrapper, or wearing a cloak without inserting arms) does not incur the prohibition penalty, because the violation is defined by the customary method of wearing. Imam Zufar dissents, arguing that any insertion of body parts into stitched clothing triggers the penalty, but the Hanafi position relies on the custom (urf) of how such garments are normally worn. Second: covering the head partially. There is consensus that covering the entire head for a full day requires dam. For partial covering, Abu Hanifa uses qiyas on shaving the head (where covering a quarter is considered significant) and on the exposure of the ‘awrah (where covering a quarter triggers obligation); he sets the threshold at one quarter of the head. Abu Yusuf looks to the reality of covering and considers the majority of the head as the threshold. The commentary also clarifies that for the time aspect, the earlier ruling (full day) applies. Note that the last sentence is incomplete at the page break.

Key Terms
حلق (ḥalq): Shaving the head, which is a prohibited act in ihram.
عورة (‘awrah): The parts of the body that must be covered; exposing them incurs sin. Here used as a basis for analogy.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (sheep/goat) required as penalty for certain violations in Hajj/Umrah.

Unconventional Wearing of Sewn Garments and Head Covering in Ihram
Ruling for unconventional wearing and head covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing sewn garments in unconventional ways during ihram and identify the threshold for covering the head that requires a dam.

Core Idea
Wearing sewn garments unconventionally is exempt from penalty; covering a quarter of the head triggers a dam.

This passage addresses two common situations for the muhrim: wearing sewn garments in a way that is not the customary manner, and covering part of the head. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: as long as the garment is not worn in the usual way (e.g., using a qamis as a scarf), no penalty applies. For head covering, the threshold is a quarter of the head according to the relied-upon view of Abu Hanifa, analogized to the quarter found in rulings on shaving and exposure of the 'awra.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses two acts: wearing a sewn garment unconventionally (e.g., using a qamis as a shawl) and covering the head partially.
For conventional wearing, penalty is clear; unconventional wearing requires analysis.
2
Locate the proof for unconventional wearing
The proof is aqli: because the garment is not worn in the customary manner, it is not considered 'wearing' the prohibited item. The text also mentions a dissenting view from Zufar.
The difficulty in keeping the garment on indicates it is not proper wearing.
3
Analyze the head covering dispute
Two positions within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to shaving and 'awra, setting the threshold at a quarter; Abu Yusuf considers most of the head (more than half) as the threshold.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's quarter.
4
Apply the rule to modern scenarios
A muhrim may use a sewn garment as a blanket or wrap without penalty. For head covering, wearing a small cap that covers a quarter of the head for a full day requires a dam.
Less than a quarter or less than a full day may require sadaqah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ لَوِ ارْتَدَى بِالْقَمِيصِ أو اتَّشَحَ بِه أو اتَّزَرَ بِالسَّرَاوِيلِ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَلْبَسُهُ لُبْسَ الْمَخِيطِ وَكَذَا لَو أَدْخَلَ مَنْكِبَيْهِ فِي الْقَبَاءِ وَلَمْ يُدْخِلْ يَدَيْهِ فِي الْكُمَّيْنِ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ لِأَنَّهُ مَا لَبِسَهُ لُبْسَ الْقَبَاءِ وَلِهَذَا يَتَكَلَّفُ فِي حِفْظِهِ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ فِي تَغْطِيَةِ الرَّأْسِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْوَقْتِ مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ وَلَا خِلَافَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا غَطَّى جَمِيعَ رَأْسِهِ يَوْمًا كَامِلًا يَجِبْ عَلَيْهِ الدَّمُ لِأَنَّهُ مَمْنُوعٌ عَنْهُ وَلَوْ غَطَّى بَعْضَ رَأْسِهِ فَالْمَرْوِيُّ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ اعْتَبَرَ الرُّبْعَ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْحَلْقِ وَالْعَوْرَةِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ سَتْرَ الْبَعْضِ اسْتِمْتَاعٌ مَقْصُودٌ يُعْتَادُهُ بَعْضُ النَّاسِ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يَعْتَبِرُ أَكْثَرَ الرَّأْسِ اعْتِبَارًا لِلْحَقِيقَةِ
And if one wraps a qamis as a scarf, or wears it over the shoulders, or wraps trousers as a loincloth, there is no harm because he did not wear them as sewn garments. Likewise, if he inserts his shoulders into a qaba but does not insert his hands into the sleeves, contrary to Zufar, because he did not wear it as a qaba is worn, and therefore he will struggle to keep it on. The measure for covering the head in terms of time is as we explained. There is no disagreement that if he covers all his head for a whole day, a dam is obligatory because it is prohibited. If he covers part of his head, the narration from Abu Hanifa is that he considers a quarter, by analogy with shaving and the 'awra. This is because covering part is a desired enjoyment that some people customarily do. From Abu Yusuf, that he considers most of the head, by consideration of the reality.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage from the sharh addresses two rulings: First, wearing sewn garments in unconventional ways during ihram. The Hanafi rule is that if a muhrim does not wear a sewn garment in the customary manner (e.g., using a qamis as a shawl, or wearing a qaba without inserting the arms), no penalty is required because it is not considered 'wearing' in the prohibited sense. This is opposed to Imam Zufar's view that penalty is due. The Hanafi proof is that the garment is not worn in the customary manner, as indicated by the difficulty in keeping it on. Second, covering the head: unanimously, covering the entire head for a full day requires a dam. For covering part of the head, Abu Hanifa analogizes to shaving a quarter of the head or uncovering a quarter of the 'awra, so covering a quarter of the head triggers a dam. Abu Yusuf considers 'most of the head' as the threshold, based on the literal majority being effectively whole. The commentary emphasizes that the quarter threshold is based on customary practice (e.g., small caps worn by Turks and Iraqis covering about a quarter). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's, as it is the basis for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
اضطباع (iḍṭibāʿ): Wearing a garment under the right armpit and throwing it over the left shoulder, commonly done in ihram.
ارتشاء (irtishāʾ): Entering the garment under the right arm and placing it on the left shoulder, similar to iḍṭibāʿ but without tawaf context.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (e.g., a sheep) required as penalty for certain violations during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what part of the head must be covered to require a dam during ihram?
A) The entire head
B) Half the head
C) One quarter of the head
D) Any part of the head

Key Takeaway
In ihram, wearing sewn garments unconventionally is penalty-free, while covering a quarter of the head (mufta bihi) for a full day necessitates a dam.

Shaving Head or Beard During Ihram: The Quarter Threshold and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling for shaving part of head/beard and disputes with Maliki and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving the head or beard during ihram (dam vs. sadaqah based on quarter threshold) and evaluate the Maliki and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
Shaving a quarter or more of the head or beard during ihram requires a dam; less requires sadaqah — custom defines completeness.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on shaving the head or beard during ihram, a common violation of ihram prohibitions. It distinguishes between shaving a quarter or more (dam) and less than a quarter (sadaqah). The school also addresses objections from Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, using custom (urf) as a key principle. Understanding this dispute helps clarify how the Hanafi school derives rulings from custom and analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: shaving a quarter or more of the head or beard triggers a dam; less than a quarter triggers sadaqah.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their positions
Imam Malik holds that only shaving the entire head or beard requires a dam. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any amount (even three hairs) requires a dam.
Both are based on different understandings of the dalil.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Malik relies on the Quranic verse 'Do not shave your heads' (al-Baqarah 196), interpreted as a prohibition of the full act. Shafi'i analogizes to cutting the plants of the Haram, where any amount is prohibited and requires a penalty.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the prohibition is general, but the penalty amount is determined by custom (urf). Shaving a quarter is customary and constitutes a complete benefit (irtifāq kāmil), so the violation is complete at a quarter. Less than that is incomplete.
This is distinguished from applying perfume to a quarter of a limb, which is not customary.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under the Hanafi school, a pilgrim who shaves a quarter of his head must offer a dam; under Maliki, only if he shaves all; under Shafi'i, for any amount, even a few hairs.

وَإِذَا حَلَقَ رُبعَ رَأْسِهِ أَوْ رُبعَ لِحْيَتِهِ فَصَاعِدًا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ فَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَّ مِنَ الرُّبْع فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَهُ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ لَا يَجِبُ إلَّا بحلق الكُلّ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجِبُ بحَلْق القَلِيْلِ اِعْتِبَارًا بِنَبَاتِ الحرَم وَلَنَا أَنَّ حَلْقَ بَعْض الرَّأْسِ ارْتِفَاقُ كَامِل لأنَّهُ مُعْتَادٌ فَتَتَكَامَلُ بِهِ الْجِنايَةُ وتَتَقَاصَرُ فِيْمَا دُونَهُ بِخَلافِ تَطِيبَ رَبعَ الْعُضْوِ لأنَّهُ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ وَكَذَا حَلْقُ بَعْض اللحية مُعْتَادُ بِالْعِرَاقِ وَأَرْضِ الْعَرَب
And if he shaves a quarter of his head or a quarter of his beard or more, then upon him is a dam. If it is less than a quarter, then upon him is sadaqah. Malik said: It is not obligatory except by shaving all. Al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory by shaving a little, by analogy with the plants of the Haram. Our proof is that shaving part of the head is a complete benefit because it is customary, so the violation is complete with it and is reduced for less than that, contrary to applying perfume to a quarter of a limb because that is not intended. Similarly, shaving part of the beard is customary in Iraq and the Arab lands.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on shaving the head or beard during ihram. The Hanafi position: if one shaves a quarter or more of the head or beard, a dam is obligatory; if less than a quarter, sadaqah (charity) is due. Imam Malik holds that only shaving the entire head or beard requires a dam, arguing from the Qur'anic verse 'Do not shave your heads' (al-Baqarah 196) which prohibits shaving the whole, not part. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that even a small amount (e.g., three hairs) triggers a dam, analogizing to cutting the plants of the Haram where any amount is penalized. The Hanafi proof is based on custom: shaving a quarter is a complete benefit (irtifāq kāmil) as it is customary (e.g., Turks shave the middle of the head, some shave the forelock). Therefore, the violation (jināyah) is complete at a quarter, and incomplete below it. This is unlike applying perfume to a quarter of a limb, which is not customary and thus not a complete benefit. The commentary explains that shaving part of the beard is also customary in Iraq and Arab lands, so the same rule applies. The mufta bihi position is the Hanafi one: quarter threshold for dam.

Key Terms
حلق (ḥalaqa): Shaving the hair of the head or beard during ihram, which is prohibited and requires a penalty.
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity, which in this context is a penalty for violations less than a quarter (typically giving food grains).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Dam (blood sacrifice)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) Nothing
D) Repeat the Hajj

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses a quarter threshold for shaving the head or beard during ihram, based on custom, and this is the mufta bihi position.

Dam for Shaving Quarter of Head or Beard in Ihram
Presents the Hanafi ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on shaving in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving head/beard in ihram, explain why the quarter threshold is used, and evaluate the proofs of Malik and Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Quarter of head/beard shaved = complete benefit = dam; less = incomplete = sadaqah.

In this lesson, we examine a classical Hanafi ruling on a common ihram issue: shaving the head or beard. The school sets a precise threshold — a quarter — based on custom and benefit. We will explore how this ruling differs from Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i and appreciate the Hanafi reliance on custom (urf) as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly is the rule? Identify the amount (quarter or more) and the penalty (dam vs sadaqah).
Quarter is the threshold; less triggers only charity.
2
Identify the opposing views
What do Malik and Shafi'i say? Note their different thresholds: full shave for Malik, any amount for Shafi'i.
Both base their views on different proofs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
How does the school justify the quarter? Understand the role of custom (urf) and complete benefit (irtifaq kamil).
The counterexample of perfuming a quarter of a limb shows the principle.
4
Compare the opposing proofs
What is Malik's proof (literal Quranic interpretation) and Shafi'i's proof (qiyas to plants)?
Note the different hermeneutics.
5
Determine the practical difference
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? How does a muhrim's action trigger different penalties in each school?
This matters for fatwa and personal practice.

چوتھائی سر یا داڑھی کائی دم ہے۔ اگر چوتھائی یہ کم کائی تو صدقہ ہے، اقوال فقہاء
وَإِذَا حَلَقَ رُبعَ رَأْسِهِ أَوْ رُبعَ لِحْيَتِهِ فَصَاعِدًا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ فَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَّ مِنَ الرُّبْع فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَهُ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ لَا يَجِبُ إلَّا بحلق الكُلّ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَجِبُ بحَلْق القَلِيْلِ اِعْتِبَارًا بِنَبَاتِ الحرَم وَلَنَا أَنَّ حَلْقَ بَعْض الرَّأْسِ ارْتِفَاقُ كَامِل لأنَّهُ مُعْتَادٌ فَتَتَكَامَلُ بِهِ الْجِنايَةُ وتَتَقَاصَرُ فِيْمَا دُونَهُ بِخَلافِ تَطِيبَ رَبعَ الْعُضْوِ لأنَّهُ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ وَكَذَا حَلْقُ بَعْض اللحية مُعْتَادُ بِالْعِرَاقِ وَأَرْضِ الْعَرَب
ترجمہ اور اگر محرم نے اپنے چوتھائی سر یا چوتھائی داڑھی یا زائد کا حلق کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اگر چوتھائی سے کم ہو تو اس پر صدقہ واجب ہے۔ اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ دم واجب نہیں ہو گا مگر کل کے حلق سے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ دم واجب ہو گا مقدار قلیل کے حلق سے بھی حرم کی گھاس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تھوڑ اسا سر مونڈنا پورا انتفاع ہے کیونکہ یہ معتاد ہے تو اسی قدر کے ساتھ جرم پورا ہو جائے گا اور اس سے کم کی صورت میں جرم ناقص ہوگا، برخلاف چوتھائی عضو کو خوشبو لگانے کے کیونکہ وہ غیر مقصود ہے۔ اور یونہی داڑھی کا کچھ حصہ مونڈ نا عراق اور عرب میں معتاد ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم نے چوتھائی سر یا چوتھائی داڑھی یا زائد کا حلق کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہو جائے گا اور اگر چوتھائی سے کم کا حلق کیا تو صدقہ واجب ہوگا ۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک وجوب دم کے لئے پورے سر یا پوری داڑھی کا حلق ضروری ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک تین بالوں کے حلق سے بھی دم واجب ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی محرم کے بالوں کو حرم کی گھاس پر قیاس کرتے ہیں یعنی جس طرح وجوب دم کے حق میں حرم کی گھاس میں قلیل و کثیر دونوں برابر ہیں اسی طرح بالوں میں بھی قلیل و کثیر دونوں برابر ہیں۔ امام مالک کا مستدل باری تعالى كا قول وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُ وَسَكُم (البقرة: ۱۹۶) ہے کیونکہ راُس کل کا نام ہے اس لئے ممنوع کل راُس کا حلق ہے نہ کہ بعض رائس کا اور جب کل راُس کا حلق ممنوع ہے تو کل راُس کے حلق سے دم واجب ہوگا نہ کہ بعض راُس کے حلق سے ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک چوتھائی سرکا حلق بھی کامل انتفاع ہے کیونکہ لوگوں کو اس کی سے کم مونڈنے کی صورت میں صدقہ واجب ہو گا۔ برخلاف اس کے کہ اگر ایک چوتھائی عضو کو خوشبو لگائی تو دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ خوشبو لگانے کے حق میں عضو کامل کا حکم وہ ہوگا جو حلق میں چوتھائی کا ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح کچھ داڑھی کا مونڈ نا اہل عراق اور اہل عرب کی عادت رہی ہے۔
If a muhrim shaves a quarter of his head or a quarter of his beard or more, then upon him is a dam; if it is less than a quarter, then upon him is sadaqah. Malik said: It is not obligatory except by shaving all. Shafi'i said: It is obligatory by shaving a little, by analogy to the plants of the Haram. Our evidence is that shaving part of the head is complete benefit because it is customary, so the violation is complete with it and falls short in what is less than it, contrary to perfuming a quarter of a limb because it is not intended. Similarly, shaving part of the beard is customary in Iraq and the land of the Arabs. Translation: And if a muhrim shaves his quarter head or quarter beard or more, then dam is wajib; if less than quarter, sadaqah is wajib. Imam Malik said: dam is not wajib except by shaving all. Imam Shafi'i said: dam is wajib even by shaving a small amount, by analogy to the plants of the Haram. Our evidence is that shaving a small part of the head is complete benefit because it is customary, so with that amount the violation is complete, and with less it is incomplete, unlike perfuming a quarter of a limb because it is not intended. Similarly, shaving some of the beard is customary in Iraq and the Arab lands. Explanation: The issue is that if a muhrim shaves a quarter of his head or quarter of his beard or more, dam is wajib; if less than quarter, sadaqah is wajib. According to Imam Malik, for dam to be wajib, shaving the entire head or entire beard is necessary. According to Imam Shafi'i, even shaving three hairs makes dam wajib. Imam Shafi'i analogizes the muhrim's hair to the plants of the Haram: just as in the Haram, the plants are equal in small and large amounts regarding dam, similarly hair. Imam Malik's proof is Allah's statement {And do not shave your heads} [2:196] because 'head' is a name for the whole, so the prohibition is for shaving the whole head, not part; so dam is only by shaving the whole. Our proof is that shaving a quarter of the head is also complete benefit because it is customary. Indeed, Turks customarily shave only the middle, and some Alawis customarily shave their foreheads. In any case, when shaving a quarter gives complete benefit, then the violation is also complete; less than quarter gives incomplete violation. Since complete violation requires dam and incomplete requires sadaqah, thus shaving quarter requires dam and less requires sadaqah. Contrary to perfuming a quarter of a limb, where dam is not wajib because for perfuming, the ruling of a whole limb is like that of a quarter in shaving. Similarly, shaving some beard is customary for Iraqis and Arabs.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ruling on shaving the head or beard while in ihram. The author first states the ruling: if a muhrim shaves a quarter or more of his head or beard, a dam (blood penalty) is wajib; if less than a quarter, only sadaqah (charity) is wajib. He then presents the views of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Imam Malik holds that dam is only wajib for shaving the entire head or beard, based on the literal meaning of the Quranic verse 'Do not shave your heads' (2:196), where 'heads' implies the whole. Imam Shafi'i holds that even a small amount, like three hairs, requires dam, by analogy to the plants of the Haram, where any amount is prohibited. The Hanafi school responds by distinguishing based on custom (urf). Shaving a quarter of the head or beard is a complete benefit (irtifaq kamil) because it is a common practice in many cultures (e.g., Turks shaving the middle of the head, Alawis shaving the forehead). Since it is a complete benefit, the violation (jinayah) is complete, requiring dam. Shaving less than a quarter is an incomplete benefit, so the violation is incomplete, requiring only sadaqah. This reasoning is supported by the counterexample of perfuming: if one perfumes a quarter of a limb, no dam is required because perfuming a quarter is not a common practice and therefore not a complete benefit. Thus, the Hanafi position is based on urf (custom) determining the threshold for a complete violation. The passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of using custom (urf) and benefit (irtifaq) to determine the threshold for penalties, in contrast to the literalist approach of Malik and the pure qiyas of Shafi'i.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving or removing hair; specifically of the head or beard in ihram.
دم (dam): Blood penalty; a sacrifice of a goat or sheep required for certain violations in ihram.
ربع (rub'): Quarter; the threshold for a complete violation in shaving head/beard.
ارتفاق (irtifaq): Benefit or advantage obtained from an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of head hair a muhrim must shave to require a dam?
A) One hair
B) A quarter of the head
C) Half of the head
D) The entire head

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses custom (urf) to define a 'complete benefit' (irtifaq kamil), setting the threshold for a dam at shaving a quarter or more of the head or beard in ihram.

Shaving the Back of the Neck and Armpits in Ihram
States Hanafi rulings on shaving back of neck and armpits with qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on shaving the entire back of the neck and one or both armpits in ihram, and explain the analogy to the pubic area.

Core Idea
Shaving an entire limb intended for hair removal in ihram requires dam; armpits are analogized to the pubic area.

The passage from Al-Hidayah deals with two specific cases of hair removal in ihram: the back of the neck and the armpits. The author establishes the obligation of dam (sacrifice) for shaving either of these, drawing an analogy (qiyas) to the pubic area. Additionally, a note about the sunnah method of plucking (natf) versus shaving (halq) is included, but the ruling remains the same.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific acts are being ruled upon? For each, what is the penalty? The passage covers shaving the entire back of the neck (dam wajib) and shaving one or both armpits (dam wajib).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof for the armpit ruling is qiyas (analogy) to the pubic area. What is the shared illa (effective cause)? Both are limbs intentionally shaved to remove discomfort and obtain comfort.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the analogy prove the ruling? The pubic area is prohibited for shaving in ihram (requires dam). Since armpits share the same purpose (intentional removal for comfort), they receive the same ruling.
This is qiyas shabahah (analogy of resemblance).
4
Note the internal Hanafi discussion
The text notes that Imam Muhammad uses 'halq' (shaving) in al-Jami' al-Saghir and 'natf' (plucking) in al-Mabsut. Both incur dam, but plucking is the sunnah. This is a difference in wording, not ruling.
The ruling is consistent across narrations.
5
Address the potential objection
Why does shaving both armpits require only one dam, not two? Because both violations are of the same type (jins), so a single penalty applies. This is analogous to using depilatory on the whole body.
This introduces a broader Hanafi principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پوری گدی منڈوائی تو دم لازم ہے، دونوں یا ایک بغل کے بال کالے تو دم لازم ہے
وَإِنْ حَلَقَ الرَّقَبَةَ كُلَّهَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ لِأَنَّهُ عُضو مَقْصُودُ بِالْحَلْقِ وَإِن حَلَقَ الإبطين أو أحَدَهُمَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَقْصُودْ بِالْحَلْقِ لِدَفَع الأذى وَنَيْلِ الرَّاحِةِ فَاشْبَهَ الْعَانَةَ ذَكَرَ فِى الْأَبْطَيْنِ الْحَلْقَ هُنَا وَفِي الْأَصْلِ التَّتَفُ وَهُوَ السُّنَهُ وَقَالَ ابْوَيُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ إِذَا حَلَقَ عُضُوا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَّ فَطَعَامُ أَرَادَ بِهِ الصَّدْرُ وَالسَّاقُ وَمَا أشبه ذلك لأنَّهُ مَقْصُودُ بِطَريقِ التَّنور فيَتَكَامُلَ بِحَلْقَ كُلَّه وَيَتَقَاصَرُ عِندَ حَلْقٍ بَعْضِه
ترجمہ اور اگر پوری گدی منڈائی تو اس پر دم واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ عضو مقصود بالحلق ہے۔ اور اگر محرم نے دونوں بغل یا ایک کو مونڈا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے کیونکہ اذیت کو دور کرنے کے لئے اور راحت کو حاصل کرنے کے لئے دونوں بغلوں میں سے ہر ایک کو بالقصد مونڈا جاتا ہے تو یہ زیر ناف کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ امام محمد نے یہاں بغلوں کے بارے میں لفظ حلق ذکر کیا اور مبسوط میں لفظ نتف (اکھاڑنا ) ذکر کیا اور یہی سنت ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف ومحمد نے کہا کہ جب ایک عضو کا حلق کیا تو اس پر دم ہے اور اگر عضو سے کم ہو تو طعام لازم ہے۔ امام محمد کی مراد سینہ، پنڈلی اور جو اس کی مانند ہے وہ ہے کیونکہ یہ نورہ لگانے کے طور پر مقصود ہے پس اس کے کل کے حلق سے جرم کامل ہو گا اور بعض کے حلق سے جرم ناقص ہوگا ۔ تشریح اگر محرم نے اپنی پوری گدی کا حلق کیا تو اس پر بھی دم جنایت واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ گدی ایسا عضو ہے جسن کو بالا رادہ مونڈا جاتا ہے چنانچہ بہت سے لوگ راحت و زینت کے لئے مونڈتے ہیں۔ اگر چہ ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور اگر محرم نے دونوں بغل یا ایک بغل کا حلق کیا تو اس پر بھی دم واجب ہے کیونکہ ہر بغل کو بالا رادہ مونڈا جاتا ہے تا کہ گندگی دور اور راحت حاصل ہوپس ہر بغل زیر ناف کے مشابہ ہو گئی ۔ یعنی جس طرح زیر ناف مونڈنے سے دم واجب ہوتا ہے اسی طرح ہر بغل میں بھی دم واجب ہوگا۔ یہاں یہ سوال ہو سکتا ہے کہ جب ہر بغل مقصود با خلق ہے تو دونوں بغلوں کو مونڈنے سے دودم واجب ہونے چاہئیں تھے حالانکہ آپ ایک ہی دم واجب کرتے ہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم کی دوجنا یتیں ایک نوع کی ہوں تو ان میں ایک ہی ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر کوئی محرم نور و ( خاص قسم کا چونه ( یعنی بال صاف کے ذریعہ اپنے پورے بدن کے بال صاف کر دے تو اس پر ایک ہی دم واجب ہوتا ہے پس اسی طرح دونوں بغل مونڈنے سے بھی ایک ہی دم واجب ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے جامع صغیر اور مبسوط کی روایتوں میں لفظی فرق بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر کی روایت میں بغلوں کے بارے میں لفظ حلق ( مونڈ نا ) ذکر کیا ہے اور مبسوط کی روایت میں لفظ نف ( بال اکھاڑ نا ) ذکر کیا ہے۔ وجوب دم کے حق میں دونوں برابر ہیں البتہ شف سنت ہے۔
If he shaves the entire back of the neck, then upon him is dam, because it is a limb intended for shaving. If he shaves the armpits or one of them, then upon him is dam, because each one of them is intended for shaving to repel harm and obtain comfort, so it resembles the pubic area. Here in the armpits he mentioned shaving, and in the original (al-Mabsut) he mentioned plucking, and that is the sunnah. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: When he shaves a limb, then upon him is dam; if it is less (than the whole limb), then food (is due). By that he meant the chest, shin, and similar parts, because they are intended by way of depilatory, so the violation is complete by shaving all of it and falls short when shaving part. Translation: If he shaves the entire back of the neck, then dam is wajib, because it is a limb intended for shaving. If a muhrim shaves both armpits or one, then dam is wajib, because each armpit is intentionally shaved to remove annoyance and gain comfort, so it resembles the pubic area. Imam Muhammad here mentioned the word 'shaving' for armpits, and in al-Mabsut he mentioned 'plucking', and that is the sunnah. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: When he shaves a limb, then dam is on him; if less than the limb, then food is due. By that they meant the chest, shin, and similar, because they are intended by way of depilatory (tanawwur), so the violation is complete by shaving all and falls short by shaving part. Explanation: If a muhrim shaves his entire back of the neck, then dam of violation is wajib, because the back of the neck is a limb that is deliberately shaved; many people shave it for comfort and adornment, although doing so is makruh. If a muhrim shaves both armpits or one armpit, then dam is wajib, because each armpit is deliberately shaved to remove dirt and gain comfort, so each armpit resembles the pubic area. Just as shaving the pubic area requires dam, similarly each armpit requires dam. Here a question may arise: if each armpit is intended for shaving, then shaving both should require two dams, but you only require one dam. The answer is that if the muhrim commits two violations of the same type, then only one penalty is due. For example, if a muhrim removes all body hair using a depilatory (nurah), then only one dam is due. Similarly, shaving both armpits requires only one dam. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned that Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir used the word 'shaving' (halq) for armpits, and in al-Mabsut he used the word 'plucking' (natf). Both are equal regarding obligation of dam, but plucking is the sunnah.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage covers additional penalties for hair removal in ihram. First, shaving the entire back of the neck (raqabah) requires dam because it is a limb that is commonly shaved intentionally for comfort and adornment, though it is makruh. Second, shaving one or both armpits also requires dam because each armpit is intentionally shaved to remove discomfort, similar to the pubic area (anah) which is a prohibited area. The author addresses a potential objection: since each armpit is a separate violation, shaving both should incur two dams. He responds that multiple violations of the same type (jins) are covered by a single penalty. This is analogous to using a depilatory on the entire body, which only requires one dam. The passage also notes a variant narration: in al-Jami' al-Saghir, Imam Muhammad uses the word 'halq' (shaving) for armpits, while in al-Mabsut he uses 'natf' (plucking). Both trigger dam, but plucking is the sunnah. Additionally, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad provide a general principle: shaving an entire limb (like chest, shin, etc.) that is intentionally removed by depilatory requires dam; shaving part requires food (sadaqah). This is consistent with the earlier ruling on head and beard.

Key Terms
رقبة (raqabah): Back of the neck; shaving it entirely in ihram requires dam.
ابط (ibt): Armpit; shaving one or both in ihram requires dam.
نتف (natf): Plucking hair; the sunnah method for armpits according to al-Mabsut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim shaves his entire back of the neck, what is the required penalty?
A) Sadaqah
B) Dam
C) Nothing, it is permissible
D) Two dams

Key Takeaway
Shaving the entire back of the neck or one/both armpits in ihram requires dam under Hanafi law, with both armpits counting as one violation.

Single Penalty for Same-Type Violations in Ihram
Explains the Hanafi rule of merging penalties for same-type violations in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that multiple violations of the same type (jins) in ihram require only one penalty, using hair removal as a case study.

Core Idea
Multiple violations of the same type in ihram merge into a single penalty.

The passage from Al-Hidayah introduces a key Hanafi principle when discussing the penalty for shaving both armpits: if a muhrim commits multiple violations of the same type (jins), only one penalty is due. This principle is illustrated by the example of using a depilatory on the entire body, which also requires only one dam. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly calculating expiations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle being stated
What is the rule that the author uses to answer the objection? The author says: 'if the muhrim commits two violations of the same type, then only one penalty is due.' This is the principle of merger (tadahkhul) for same-type violations.
2
Find the example given
The author gives the example of using nurah (depilatory) on the whole body. Even though multiple limbs are involved, only one dam is due because all hair removal is of the same type (jins).
3
Apply the principle to the armpits case
Both armpits are of the same type (both are hair removal from armpits). Therefore, shaving both armpits requires only one dam, not two.
4
Distinguish different types
The principle applies only when the violations are of the same type. For example, shaving the head vs. shaving the beard may be different types (due to different rulings). The passage does not define 'type' explicitly, but the context suggests that same limb or same category (hair removal) constitutes one type.
5
Consider the scope
The principle is not limited to hair removal; it applies generally to violations in ihram (e.g., multiple instances of breaking a prohibition of the same kind).

Source Text

Commentary
This passage covers additional penalties for hair removal in ihram. First, shaving the entire back of the neck (raqabah) requires dam because it is a limb that is commonly shaved intentionally for comfort and adornment, though it is makruh. Second, shaving one or both armpits also requires dam because each armpit is intentionally shaved to remove discomfort, similar to the pubic area (anah) which is a prohibited area. This is consistent with the earlier ruling on head and beard.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Type or category; violations of the same jins merge in penalty.
نورہ (nurah): A lime-based depilatory used to remove body hair; used as an example of a single violation covering the whole body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi principle in this lesson, how many penalties are due if a muhrim uses perfume on his left arm and then on his right arm?

Shaving the Nape and Armpits in Ihram: Qiyas and Limb Distinction
States rulings for shaving nape/armpits and explains Sahibayn's limb-based distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for shaving a complete limb vs. part of a limb during Ihram and explain the qiyas to the pubic area.

Core Idea
Shaving a complete limb during Ihram requires dam; partial shaving requires sadaqah.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common Ihram violation: shaving body hair beyond the allowed restrictions. The ruling distinguishes between shaving an entire limb (like the nape, armpit, chest, or shin) and shaving only part of it. Using qiyas to the pubic area, the Hanafi school imposes a dam for complete limbs and sadaqah for partial removal. We will explore the proof, the limb definition, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State what act triggers a dam and what act triggers sadaqah according to the passage.
The nape and armpits are explicitly mentioned as complete limbs.
2
Trace the qiyas proof
Find the analogy (qiyas) used: the armpit is compared to the pubic area. Identify the illa (effective cause).
The illa is that both are intentionally shaved for comfort and hygiene.
3
Define a complete limb (udw)
Understand how Sahibayn define a limb: chest, shin, thigh — parts customarily depilated with nurah.
Not every body part is a limb; the definition is based on urf (custom).
4
Apply the distinction
Determine the penalty for a scenario: shaving an entire limb = dam; shaving part of a limb = sadaqah.
Multiple violations of the same type merge into one dam.

Source Text

پوری گدی منڈوائی تو دم لازم ہے، دونوں یا ایک بغل کے بال کالے تو دم لازم ہے
وَإِنْ حَلَقَ الرَّقَبَةَ كُلَّهَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ لِأَنَّهُ عُضو مَقْصُودُ بِالْحَلْقِ وَإِن حَلَقَ الإبطين أو أحَدَهُمَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مَقْصُودْ بِالْحَلْقِ لِدَفَع الأذى وَنَيْلِ الرَّاحِةِ فَاشْبَهَ الْعَانَةَ ذَكَرَ فِى الْأَبْطَيْنِ الْحَلْقَ هُنَا وَفِي الْأَصْلِ التَّتَفُ وَهُوَ السُّنَهُ وَقَالَ ابْوَيُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ إِذَا حَلَقَ عُضُوا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمُ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَّ فَطَعَامُ أَرَادَ بِهِ الصَّدْرُ وَالسَّاقُ وَمَا أشبه ذلك لأنَّهُ مَقْصُودُ بِطَريقِ التَّنور فيَتَكَامُلَ بِحَلْقَ كُلَّه وَيَتَقَاصَرُ عِندَ حَلْقٍ بَعْضِه
