Looking and Touching One's Wife with Desire in Ihram
Ruling on looking/touching wife with desire in ihram and Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim looking at or touching his wife with desire in ihram, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and apply the Hanafi distinction between jima' and other sexual acts.

Core Idea
In ihram, only actual intercourse invalidates Hajj; lesser acts require a dam but not invalidation.

This lesson examines a specific dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the consequences of a muhrim engaging in sexual acts short of intercourse. The Hanafi school maintains a clear hierarchy: only actual jima' invalidates the Hajj, while other prohibited acts, such as kissing or touching with desire, require a sacrificial dam. Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes these acts to fasting, arguing that any act leading to emission should invalidate ihram. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens one's appreciation of how each school derives rulings from the core texts and the principles of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on looking
Identify the ruling for looking at the wife's private part with desire and emitting maniy. Note that the text says 'la shay 'alayh' – no penalty.
This is because looking is not considered an act of jima'.
2
State the Hanafi position on kissing/touching
Identify the ruling for kissing or touching with desire. The text says 'fa 'alayhi dam' – a dam is required, whether or not emission occurs.
The dam is wajib due to the pleasure-seeking aspect.
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any act leading to emission invalidates ihram, by analogy (qiyas) to fasting, where emission breaks the fast.
The illa (effective cause) is fulfillment of desire through emission.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the qiyas
The Hanafi school rejects the analogy because the rulings for Hajj and fasting differ fundamentally. In Hajj, invalidation is specific to jima', not to emission. In fasting, any fulfillment of desire invalidates.
Thus, the same act (e.g., kissing without emission) would break a fast but does not invalidate Hajj.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi, a muhrim who kisses and emits must offer a dam but his Hajj is valid; under Shafi'i, his Hajj becomes invalid and must be repeated with a sacrifice.
This difference affects both the obligation and the validity of the pilgrimage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فَإِنْ نَظَرَ إِلى فَرْجِ امْرَأَتِهِ بِشَهْوَةٍ فَأَمُنى لَا شَيْء عَلَيْهِ لأنَّ الْمُحَرَّمَ هُوَ الْحِمَاعُ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ فَصَارَ كَمَا لَوْ تَفَكَّر فأمنى وإِن قَبْلَ أوْلَمسَ بِشَهُوةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَم وَفِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ يَقُولُ إِذَا مَسَّ بِشَهْوَةٍ فَأَمْنِى وَلَا فَرُقَ بَيْنَ مَا إِذَا أَنزَلَ أَوْ لَم يَنزِلُ ذَكرَهُ فِي الأصْلِ وَكَذَا الْجَوَابُ فِي الْجَمَاعِ فيما دُونَ الْفَرَج وَعَنِ الشَّافِعِى أَنَّهُ يَفْسُدُ إحْرَامُهُ فِى جَميعِ ذَلِكَ إِذَا أَنزَلَ وَاعْتَبَرَهُ بِالصَّوْمِ وَلَنَا أنَّ فَسَادَ الْحَجَ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْجِمَاعِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَفْسُدُ بِسَائِرِ الْمَخْطُورَاتِ وَهَذَا لَيْسَ بِجمَاع مَقْصُودٍ فَلا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْجِمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ فِيْهِ مَعْنَى الْإِسْتَمَاع وَالْارْتَفَاقِ بِالْمَرْأَةِ وَ ذُلِكَ مَخطُورُ الإِحْرَام فَلَيْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ بِخِلافِ الصَّوْمِ لأنَّ المُحَرّمَ فِيهِ قَضَاءُ الشَّهْوَةِ وَلَا يَحْصُلُ بدون الانْزَالِ فِيْمَا دُونَ الْفَرْج
Section: If he looks at his wife's private part with desire and emits maniy, there is nothing upon him, because what is prohibited is sexual intercourse, and it did not occur. So it is as if he thought and emitted. And if he kisses or touches with desire, then a dam is upon him. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it says: When he touches with desire and emits maniy, there is no difference between whether he emits or not; he mentioned this in al-Asl. And similarly, the answer is for intercourse less than the private part. From al-Shafi'i, that his ihram is invalidated in all of that if he emits, and he analogizes it to fasting. Our evidence is that the invalidation of Hajj is attached to sexual intercourse, and for this reason it is not invalidated by other prohibited acts. And this is not intended intercourse, so what is attached to intercourse does not attach to it. However, there is in it the meaning of seeking pleasure and benefiting from the woman, and that is prohibited in ihram, so a dam is incumbent upon him, unlike fasting, because what is prohibited in fasting is fulfilling desire, and that does not occur without emission in what is less than the private part.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i regarding the penalty for a muhrim who looks at or touches his wife with desire during ihram. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) If the muhrim looks at his wife's private part with desire and emits maniy (but without physical contact or with contact less than intercourse), there is no penalty, because the prohibition in ihram is specifically on actual sexual intercourse (jima'), and this act is not intercourse. It is likened to merely thinking and emitting, which carries no penalty. (2) If he kisses or touches with desire, then a dam (sacrifice of a goat) is wajib, regardless of whether emission occurs. This is based on the principle that such acts, while not intercourse, involve seeking pleasure and benefiting from the wife, which is prohibited in ihram. The text also notes that in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Asl, the ruling for touching with desire (even without emission) is that a dam is required. Similarly, for intercourse less than full penetration (i.e., without entering the vagina), the ruling is also a dam, not invalidation of ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: he holds that any of these acts, if accompanied by emission, invalidates the ihram altogether, by analogy with fasting where emission breaks the fast. The Hanafi response rejects this analogy, arguing that Hajj is invalidated only by actual sexual intercourse (jima'), not by other prohibited acts. Since these acts are not intended intercourse (jima' maqsud), they do not carry the gravest consequence of ihram invalidation. However, because they involve prohibited pleasure-seeking, a dam is sufficient as a penalty. This is unlike fasting, where the prohibition is on fulfilling desire itself, and emission without intercourse does fulfill desire, thus invalidating the fast. In ihram, the primary prohibition is on intercourse, so lesser acts carry lesser penalties.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a goat) required as a penalty for certain violations during ihram.
جماع مقصود (jima' maqsud): Actual sexual intercourse involving penetration of the private part.
الاستمتاع والارتفاق (al-istimta' wa al-irtifaq): Seeking pleasure and benefiting from the wife, which is prohibited in ihram but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a muhrim kisses his wife with desire in ihram and emits?
A) His ihram is invalidated and he must repeat Hajj
B) Nothing is required
C) He must offer a dam (sacrifice)
D) He must fast three days

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, only actual sexual intercourse invalidates ihram; other sexual acts with desire require a dam but do not nullify the pilgrimage.

Penalty for Muhrim: Feeding vs. Ownership (Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on feeding vs. ownership for muhrim's penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the penalty for a muhrim who cannot fast, identify the linguistic basis (sadaqah vs. it'am) for the dispute, and apply the mufta bihi position to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Sadaqah requires ownership (tamlik); it'am requires only feeding — the Quranic word determines the penalty's condition.

When a muhrim (one in ihram) cannot fast the required penalty days, he may give food. But what exactly must he give? Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, both giants of the Hanafi school, disagree on whether mere feeding suffices or whether ownership must be transferred. This lesson unpacks their linguistic and analogical arguments and identifies the relied-upon opinion for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and obligation
The muhrim is excused from fasting and chooses the option of giving food (sadaqah) as a penalty. Identify the Quranic basis: 'or a sadaqah' (2:196).
The penalty is wajib, not fard.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf holds that feeding six poor people morning and evening suffices. His proof is qiyas on kaffarat al-yamin, where the Quran uses 'it'am' (feeding).
He treats the two expiations as analogous.
3
State Muhammad's position and proof
Muhammad holds that feeding is insufficient; ownership of three sa' of wheat to six poor people is required. His proof is the literal meaning of 'sadaqah', which implies transfer of ownership (tamlik).
He distinguishes between sadaqah and it'am.
4
Analyze the key linguistic distinction
The Quran uses 'sadaqah' in the penalty verse (2:196) and 'it'am' in the oath expiation verse (5:89). Sadaqah means giving ownership without compensation; it'am means making food available (ibahah).
This linguistic difference is decisive in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) favors Muhammad's view, ruling that ownership is required. This is the operative position for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
Abu Yusuf's qiyas is considered incorrect because the two texts use different words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ اخْتَارَ الطَّعَامَ أَجْزَأَهُ فِيهِ التَّعْدِيَةُ وَالتَّعْشِيَّةُ عِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ اعْتِبَارًا بِكَفَّارَةِ الْيَمِينِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ لَا يُجْزِيهِ لِأَنَّ الصَّدَقَةَ تَنْبَنِي عَنْ التَّمْلِيكِ وَهُوَ الْمَذْكُورُ

ترجمہ: اور اگر معذور محرم نے کھانا دینا اختیار کر لیا تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس کو صبح کا کھانا کھلانا اور شام کا کھانا کھلانا کافی ہو گا۔ کفارہ یمین پر قیاس کیا گیا ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ صدقہ خبر دیتا ہے تملیک کی اور قرآن میں یہی صدقہ مذکور ہے۔

تشریح: مسئلہ، اگر معذور محرم نے صدقہ دینا اختیار کیا تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ کافی ہے کہ وہ چھ مساکین کو صبح وشام کھانا کھلا دے، ابو یوسف اس کو کفارہ یمین پر قیاس کرتے ہیں پس جس طرح کفارہ یمین میں صبح و شام مساکین کو کھانا کھلانا کافی ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی کھانا کھلانا کافی ہوگا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک کھانا کھلانا کافی نہیں ہے بلکہ چھ مساکین کو تین صاع گندم کا مالک کر دینا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ قرآن پاک میں أَوْ صَدَقَةٌ میں لفظ صدقہ مذکور ہے اور صدقہ کے لغوی معنی بلا عوض مالک کو دینے کے ہیں اس لئے مساکین کو مالک کر دینا ضروری ہے۔ برخلاف کھانا کھلانے کے کہ وہ تو مباح کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کا کفارہ یمین پر قیاس درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کفارہ یمین میں قرآن پاک میں لفظ اطعام مذکور ہے۔ اور لفظ اطعام اباحت کا فائدہ دیتا ہے نہ کہ تملیک کا۔ اس لئے کفارہ یمین میں کھانا کھلانا کافی ہوگا مگر بطور جزاء صدقہ کرنے میں کھانا کھلانا کافی نہ ہوگا۔
And if he chooses feeding, then feeding morning and evening suffices him according to Abu Yusuf, by analogy to the expiation of an oath; and according to Muhammad it does not suffice him because sadaqah is based on ownership, and that [ownership] is what is mentioned [in the Quran].

Translation: And if the excused muhrim chooses to give food, then according to Abu Yusuf it is sufficient for him to feed morning and evening. It is analogized to the expiation of an oath. And according to Imam Muhammad it is not sufficient, because sadaqah indicates ownership, and in the Quran this very sadaqah is mentioned.

Explanation: The issue: If the excused muhrim chooses to give charity, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is sufficient that he feeds six needy persons morning and evening. Abu Yusuf analogizes this to the expiation of an oath. Just as in the expiation of an oath, feeding morning and evening is sufficient, similarly here feeding is sufficient. And according to Imam Muhammad, feeding is not sufficient; rather, it is necessary to give ownership of three sa' of wheat to six needy persons. Because in the Holy Quran, the word 'sadaqah' is mentioned in 'or a sadaqah', and the lexical meaning of sadaqah is to give ownership without compensation, so it is necessary to make the needy owners. Unlike feeding, which is merely making permissible (mubah). Imam Abu Yusuf's analogy to the expiation of an oath is not correct. Because in the expiation of an oath, the word 'it'am' (feeding) is mentioned in the Quran, and the word 'it'am' gives the benefit of permissibility (ibahah), not ownership. Therefore, in the expiation of an oath, feeding is sufficient, but as a penalty of sadaqah, feeding is not sufficient.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the penalty (fidyah) for a muhrim who is unable to fast (e.g., due to shaving hair) and chooses to give food instead. The text presents the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. According to Abu Yusuf, it is sufficient to feed six poor persons morning and evening, based on qiyas on kaffarat al-yamin (expiation of an oath). According to Muhammad, mere feeding is insufficient; he requires giving ownership (tamlik) of three sa' of wheat (approximately 7.56 kg) to six persons, because the Quran uses the word 'sadaqah' which implies transfer of ownership, not just feeding. The commentator then favors Muhammad's view, arguing that the wording in the Quran for the penalty is 'sadaqah' (ownership), while the word for kaffarat al-yamin is 'it'am' (feeding), so each analogy should be limited to its own context.

Key Terms
صَدَقَة (sadaqah): In this context, it refers to the penalty (fidyah) given by a muhrim who cannot fast, mentioned in the Quran as 'or a sadaqah'. The dispute centers on whether sadaqah implies ownership or mere feeding.
إِطْعَام (it'am): Feeding, used in the context of kaffarat al-yamin. According to Hanafi, it'am means making food available (ibahah), not necessarily transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is required when a muhrim chooses to give food as a penalty?
A) Feeding six poor people morning and evening
B) Giving ownership of three sa' of wheat to six poor people
C) Feeding ten poor people once
D) Slaughtering a goat

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the word 'sadaqah' requires ownership (tamlik), while 'it'am' requires only feeding; therefore, the muhrim's fidyah must involve transfer of ownership, not mere feeding.

Nullification of Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Acts Short of Intercourse
Hanafi rules on acts short of intercourse and dispute with Shafi'i on nullification of ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that only actual intercourse nullifies ihram and explain why kissing, touching, or ma duna al-farj incur a dam but do not invalidate hajj.

Core Idea
In ihram, nullification only applies to actual intercourse; other sexual acts incur a dam.

A muhrim (one in ihram) might engage in acts like looking, kissing, or touching with desire, or even intercourse less than full penetration. The Hanafi school distinguishes these sharply from actual intercourse (jima'). This lesson unpacks the rulings and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who analogizes ihram to fasting. Understanding the precise prohibition and its penalty is essential for correct hajj performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
List the acts discussed: looking at the wife's private part, kissing, touching, and ma duna al-farj (intercourse less than full penetration). For each, state the Hanafi ruling: either no penalty, dam, or nullification.
Looking without touching incurs no penalty; kissing/touching/ma duna al-farj incur dam; only actual jima' nullifies.
2
Distinguish Nullification vs Penalty
Explain why only actual intercourse nullifies ihram: the prohibition in ihram is on the act of jima' itself, not on desire fulfillment. Other acts involve pleasure (istimta') but are not jima', so they are punishable by dam but do not break ihram.
Compare with fasting: the prohibition is on fulfilling desire, so discharge nullifies fasting. The different underlying prohibitions yield different rulings.
3
Examine the Shafi'i Analogy
State the Shafi'i position: any sexual act with discharge nullifies ihram, based on qiyas to fasting. Identify the common element (discharge) and the analogized ruling.
The Shafi'i view uses a general analogy; the Hanafi view restricts nullification to jima'.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Rebuttal
Analyze the Hanafi response: the analogy fails because the 'illa (cause) differs. In fasting, the prohibition is on qada' al-shahwah; in ihram, on jima'. Acts short of jima' are not included in the nullification ruling, but they entail a penalty due to the element of pleasure.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi—dam, hajj valid; Shafi'i—hajj invalid, requires camel sacrifice and repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فَإِنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى فَرْجِ امْرَأَتِهِ بِشَهْوَةٍ فَأَمْنَى لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ الْمُحَرَّمَ هُوَ الْجِمَاعُ وَلَمْ يُوجَدْ فَصَارَ كَمَا لَوْ تَفَكَّرَ فَأَمْنَى وَإِنْ قَبَّلَ أَوْ لَمَسَ بِشَهْوَةٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَفِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ يَقُولُ إِذَا مَسَّ بِشَهْوَةٍ فَأَمْنَى وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ مَا إِذَا أَنْزَلَ أَوْ لَمْ يُنْزِلْ ذَكَرَهُ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَكَذَا الْجَوَابُ فِي الْجِمَاعِ فِيمَا دُونَ الْفَرْجِ وَعَنِ الشَّافِعِيِّ أَنَّهُ يَفْسُدُ إِحْرَامُهُ فِي جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ إِذَا أَنْزَلَ وَاعْتَبَرَهُ بِالصَّوْمِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ فَسَادَ الْحَجِّ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْجِمَاعِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَفْسُدُ بِسَائِرِ الْمَخْطُورَاتِ وَهَذَا لَيْسَ بِجِمَاعٍ مَقْصُودٍ فَلَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ مَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْجِمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ فِيهِ مَعْنَى الِاسْتِمْتَاعِ وَالِارْتِفَاقِ بِالْمَرْأَةِ وَذَلِكَ مَخْطُورُ الْإِحْرَامِ فَلَيَزَمُهُ الدَّمُ بِخِلَافِ الصَّوْمِ لِأَنَّ الْمُحَرَّمَ فِيهِ قَضَاءُ الشَّهْوَةِ وَلَا يَحْصُلُ بِدُونِ الْإِنْزَالِ فِيمَا دُونَ الْفَرْجِ

ترجمہ: فصل ۔ پس اگر محرم نے اپنی بیوی کی شرمگاہ کی طرف شہوت کے ساتھ نظر کی اور انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ (احرام میں ) جس کو حرام کیا گیا ہے وہ جماع ہے اور جماع پایا نہیں گیا۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے تصور جاناں کیا اور انزال ہو گیا۔ اور اگر محرم نے شہوت کے ساتھ بوسہ لیا یا چھوا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں فرماتے ہیں کہ جب شہوت کے ساتھ چھوا پھر انزال ہو گیا اور کوئی فرق نہیں اس صورت میں کہ انزال ہوا یا انزال نہیں ہوا اس کو مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور یہی حکم شرمگاہ کے علاوہ میں جماع کا ہے۔ اور امام شافعی سے ایک روایت ہے کہ ان تمام صورتوں میں اس کا احرام فاسد ہو جائے گا اور اس کو روزہ پر قیاس کیا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج کا فاسد ہونا جماع کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور اسی وجہ سے تمام ممنوعات سے حج فاسد نہیں ہوتا اور یہ فعل جماع مقصود نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اس کے ساتھ وہ حکم متعلق نہیں ہو گا جو جماع کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ مگر اس میں لطف اندوز اور عورت کے ساتھ لذت حاصل کرنے کے معنی ہیں اور یہ ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر دم لازم ہو گا۔ برخلاف روزہ کے۔ کیونکہ روزہ میں شہوت پوری کرنا حرام کیا گیا ہے اور شرمگاہ کے علاوہ میں بغیر انزال کے یہ بات حاصل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے اپنی بیوی یا کسی دوسری عورت کے فرج داخل کی طرف شہوت کے ساتھ دیکھا اور انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر دم وغیرہ کوئی کفارہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ احرام کی حالت میں جماع حرام کیا گیا ہے اور جماع پایا نہیں گیا اس لئے کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کوئی محرم کسی حسینہ جمیلہ کا تصور کر کے بیٹھ گیا اور انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اسی طرح فرج داخل کی طرف نظر کرنے کی صورت میں بھی کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ جماع کہتے ہیں عورت و مرد کا اکٹھا ہو صورتاً اور معنی شہوت پوری کرنا۔ صورت جماع تو یہ ہے کہ مرد اپنے عضو تناسل کو عورت کی شرمگاہ میں داخل کر دے اور معنی جماع انزال ہے۔ اور اگر محرم نے شہوت کے ساتھ عورت کا بوسہ لے لیا یا اس کو چھوا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے خواہ انزال ہو یا انزال نہ ہو۔ مبسوط میں یہی مذکور ہے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں انزال کی شرط ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اگر شہوت کے ساتھ چھوا اور انزال ہو گیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے۔ جامع صغیر کی روایت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر انزال نہ ہوا تو محرم پر دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ محرم نے اگر مادون الفرج میں یعنی ران وغیرہ میں جماع کیا تو بھی اس پر دم واجب ہو جائے گا خواہ انزال ہوا ہو یا انزال نہ ہوا ہو جیسا کہ مبسوط کی روایت ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی سے مروی ہے کہ ان تمام صورتوں میں یعنی شہوت کے ساتھ بوسہ لینے میں چھونے اور مادون الفرج میں جماع کرنے میں اگر انزال ہو گیا تو اس کا احرام فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی نے احرام کو روزے پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی جس طرح مذکورہ چیزوں سے روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے بشرطیکہ انزال ہوا ہو اسی طرح ان چیزوں سے احرام بھی فاسد ہو جائے گا۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج، جماع سے فاسد ہوتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جماع کے علاوہ دوسرے ممنوعات سے حج فاسد نہیں ہوتا۔ مثلاً سلا ہوا کپڑا پہننے اور خوشبو وغیرہ کا استعمال کرنے سے حج فاسد نہیں ہوتا اور یہ مذکورہ چیزیں یعنی چھونا، بوسہ لینا اور مادون الفرج میں جماع کرنا جماع مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک طرح کا استلذاذ ہے۔ پس جب یہ چیزیں جماع نہیں تو ان کے ساتھ فساد حج بھی متعلق نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ جماع سے فساد حج متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں عورت کے ساتھ لذت حاصل کرنے کے معنی موجود ہیں اور عورت کے ساتھ لذت حاصل کرنا احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے ہے اس لئے اس پر دم واجب ہو گا۔ برخلاف روزہ کے کیونکہ روزہ کے اندر شہوت پوری کرنا حرام ہے اور مادون الفرج میں بغیر انزال کے شہوت پوری کرنا حاصل نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے بغیر انزال کے تو روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوگا البتہ اگر انزال ہو گیا تو روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔
Section: If he looks at his wife's private part with desire and discharges, there is nothing upon him, because the prohibited thing is intercourse and it did not occur, so it becomes like if he thought [and] discharged. And if he kisses or touches with desire, then he owes a dam. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, he says: When he touches with desire and discharges, and there is no difference between whether he had ejaculation or not, he mentioned it in al-Asl. And likewise the answer regarding intercourse less than the private part. And from al-Shafi'i that his ihram is corrupted in all of that if he ejaculates, and he analogized it to fasting. And our proof is that the corruption of hajj is connected to intercourse, and for this reason it is not corrupted by other prohibited matters. And this is not intended intercourse, so what is connected to intercourse does not attach to it, except that it contains the meaning of enjoyment and benefiting from the woman, and that is prohibited in ihram, so the dam becomes necessary upon him, contrary to fasting, because in fasting what is prohibited is fulfilling desire, and it is not attained without ejaculation in less than the private part.

Translation: Section: So if a muhrim looked at his wife's private part with desire and discharged, nothing is necessary upon him. Because in ihram, what is prohibited is intercourse, and intercourse did not occur. So it becomes like he imagined and discharged. And if a muhrim kissed or touched with desire, then a dam is obligatory. And in Jami' al-Saghir, it is said: When he touched with desire and then discharged, and there is no difference between whether he discharged or not, it is mentioned in al-Mabsut. And this ruling is for intercourse less than the private part. And from Imam Shafi'i it is narrated that in all these cases his ihram becomes corrupt if he discharges, and he analogized it to fasting. And our proof is that the corruption of hajj is related to intercourse, and for this reason hajj is not corrupted by all prohibitions, and this act is not intended intercourse. Therefore, the ruling that attaches to intercourse does not attach to it. But in it there is the sense of enjoyment and deriving pleasure from a woman, and that is prohibited. Therefore, a dam becomes necessary. Contrary to fasting, because in fasting, fulfilling desire is prohibited, and without discharge in less than the private part, this is not attained.

Explanation: If a muhrim looked at the inside of the private part of his wife or another woman with desire and discharged, then no dam or other penalty is wajib. Because in the state of ihram, intercourse is prohibited, and intercourse did not occur, so nothing is wajib. And it becomes like if a muhrim sat imagining a beautiful woman and discharged, then nothing is wajib. Similarly, in the case of looking at the inside of the private part, nothing is wajib. Intercourse is said to be the joining of man and woman in form and the fulfillment of desire in meaning. The form of intercourse is that the man inserts his penis into the woman's private part, and the meaning of intercourse is discharge. And if a muhrim kissed a woman with desire or touched her, then a dam is wajib, whether he discharged or not. This is mentioned in al-Mabsut. And in Jami' al-Saghir, the condition of discharge is mentioned, so it says: If he touched with desire and discharged, then a dam is wajib. From the narration of Jami' al-Saghir, it appears that if he did not discharge, then a dam is not wajib. Sahib al-Hidayah says: If a muhrim engaged in intercourse less than the private part, i.e., in the thigh etc., then also a dam becomes wajib, whether he discharged or not, as is the narration of al-Mabsut. It is narrated from Imam Shafi'i that in all these cases, i.e., kissing with desire, touching, and intercourse less than the private part, if discharge occurred, then his ihram becomes corrupt. Imam Shafi'i analogized ihram to fasting, i.e., just as fasting becomes invalid due to these matters if discharge occurs, similarly ihram becomes invalid.

Our proof is that hajj is corrupted by intercourse. This is the reason that hajj is not corrupted by other prohibitions, e.g., wearing sewn clothes or using perfume. And these mentioned things, i.e., touching, kissing, and intercourse less than the private part, are not intended intercourse, but rather a kind of pleasure. So when these things are not intercourse, corruption of hajj is not attached to them, as it is attached to intercourse. However, it is necessary that there is the meaning of deriving pleasure from a woman in these things, and deriving pleasure from a woman is among the prohibitions of ihram, so a dam is wajib. Contrary to fasting, because in fasting, fulfilling desire is prohibited, and fulfilling desire without discharge in less than the private part is not attained. Therefore, without discharge, the fast is not corrupted, but if discharge occurs, then the fast becomes corrupted.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on various sexual acts short of full intercourse that a muhrim may commit. It begins by stating that looking at the wife's private part with desire, even if it leads to discharge, incurs no penalty because the act of looking itself is not intercourse, and the discharge alone is not the prohibited act in ihram (unlike fasting). Then it addresses kissing and touching with desire: these require a dam (sacrifice of a goat) regardless of discharge, because they involve direct pleasurable contact. The text notes a difference within the Hanafi school: according to al-Jami' al-Saghir, touching requires discharge for a dam; according to al-Mabsut, no distinction is made. The same ruling applies for intercourse less than full penetration (ma dun al-farj), e.g., between thighs: a dam is due whether or not discharge occurs. The Hanafi school then contrasts its view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that any of these acts if accompanied by discharge invalidates the ihram entirely, analogizing it to fasting. The Hanafi response is that invalidation of hajj is specifically tied to actual intercourse (jima'), not to mere gratifying acts, because the prohibition in ihram is on the act of copulation, not on the fulfillment of desire per se. However, because these acts involve pleasure, they are still prohibited and require a dam as a penalty, but they do not break the ihram. The passage further explains that fasting is different because its prohibition is on fulfilling desire, which is achieved with discharge, whereas in ihram the prohibition is on the physical act of intercourse.

Key Terms
جِمَاع (jima'): Actual intercourse involving insertion of the penis into the vagina. This is the only act that nullifies ihram according to Hanafi.
مَادُونَ الْفَرْج (ma duna al-farj): Intercourse less than full penetration, e.g., between thighs or any part other than the vagina. Hanafi: this incurs a dam but does not nullify ihram.
دَم (dam): A penalty of slaughtering a sheep or goat, required for certain violations of ihram (e.g., kissing, touching with desire, ma dun al-farj).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim kisses his wife with desire and does not have discharge, what is the ruling?
A) His hajj is nullified and he must repeat it
B) He owes a dam (sacrifice) but his hajj remains valid
C) No penalty is required because there was no discharge
D) He must fast three days

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, only actual sexual intercourse (jima') nullifies Ihram; other sexual acts with desire require a dam but do not invalidate Hajj.

Intercourse Before Wuquf: Hajj Invalid but Must Continue
Ruling on intercourse before Wuquf with evidence and Shafi'i divergence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse before Wuquf, identify the required penance, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Intercourse before Arafat corrupts Hajj, but you must complete it and sacrifice a sheep.

This lesson addresses a severe violation in Hajj: sexual intercourse before the essential rite of standing at Arafat. The Hanafi school rules that the Hajj becomes corrupt but must still be completed; after completion, a sheep must be sacrificed and the Hajj repeated the following year. This ruling is based on a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ. The Shafi'i school differs, requiring a camel instead of a sheep. We will examine the proof and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that the act is intercourse before standing at Arafat while in ihram for Hajj. The ruling: the Hajj becomes corrupt (fasid).
Corrupt means invalid but must be completed according to Hanafi.
2
State the required penances
List the three consequences: (1) continue the Hajj to completion, (2) sacrifice a sheep (shaat), (3) repeat Hajj the following year.
3
Examine the dalil (proof)
Read the hadith: the Prophet ﷺ was asked about a couple who had intercourse in ihram. He commanded: 'They shed blood (sacrifice), continue their Hajj, and repeat it next year.'
The Hanafi school takes this hadith as the primary evidence.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i requires a camel (badanah) instead of a sheep. The Hanafi school adheres to the explicit hadith.
The difference is the type of animal: sheep vs camel.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi pilgrim sacrifices a sheep; a Shafi'i pilgrim sacrifices a camel. The cost and availability differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ جَامَعَ فِي أَحَدِ السَّيْلَيْنِ قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ فَسَدَ حَجُّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ وَيَمْضِي فِي الْحَجِّ كَمَا يَمْضِي مَنْ لَمْ يَفْسُدْ حَجُّهُ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ مَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُئِلَ عَمَّنْ وَاقَعَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهُمَا مُحْرِمَانِ بِالْحَجِّ قَالَ يُرِيقَانِ دَمًا وَيَمْضِيَانِ فِي حَجَّتِهِمَا وَعَلَيْهِمَا الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ وَهَكَذَا نُقِلَ عَنْ جَمَاعَةٍ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ تَجِبُ بُدَنَةٌ
If he has intercourse in one of the two passes before standing at Arafat, his hajj is corrupted, and upon him is a sheep, and he continues in the hajj just as one whose hajj is not corrupted continues. And the basis for that is what is narrated: that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked about one who had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram for hajj. He said: 'They shed blood (sacrifice), and they continue in their hajj, and upon them is the hajj next year.' And thus it is transmitted from a group of the Companions. And al-Shafi'i said: A camel is obligatory.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage deals with the severe case of a muhrim who engages in full sexual intercourse before the essential rite of standing at Arafat. According to the Hanafi school, this act corrupts the hajj, meaning it becomes invalid. However, the pilgrim must not abandon the rites; he must continue completing the remaining acts of hajj. After completing it, he owes a penance: slaughtering a sheep (shaat) and repeating the entire hajj the following year. This ruling is based on a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about a couple who had intercourse while in ihram for hajj. He commanded them to sacrifice a sheep and continue their hajj, but to repeat it next year. The Hanafi school follows this hadith. The passage also notes that Imam al-Shafi'i differs, holding that a camel (badanah) is required instead of a sheep. This difference is significant in practice.

Key Terms
شَاة (shaat): A sheep or goat as a sacrifice.
بُدَنَة (badanah): A camel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the required sacrifice for a muhrim who has intercourse before Wuquf?
A) A camel (badanah)
B) A sheep (shaat)
C) A cow
D) Fasting three days

Key Takeaway
Intercourse before Wuquf corrupts Hajj but requires continuation, a sheep sacrifice, and repetition next year; the Hanafi school follows the explicit hadith against the Shafi'i camel requirement.

Muhrim's Intimate Acts: Kissing and Touching with Desire
Discusses Hanafi ruling on muhrim's acts besides intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim's kissing or touching with desire, explain why it does not invalidate ihram, and distinguish the Shafi'i position with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Kissing or touching with desire by a muhrim requires a dam but does not invalidate hajj.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effect of sexual acts short of intercourse during ihram. The Hanafi school distinguishes between acts that invalidate the pilgrimage (only actual intercourse) and acts that merely require expiation. The basis of this distinction lies in the nature of the prohibitions in hajj versus fasting. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of ihram violations and their legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core Hanafi ruling for a muhrim who kisses or touches with desire: a dam (sheep) is wajib, and the hajj remains valid.
The text mentions al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir; the mufta bihi does not require ejaculation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that these acts, if accompanied by ejaculation, invalidate ihram entirely.
The Shafi'i view analogizes ihram to fasting.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i qiyas: just as kissing/touching with ejaculation invalidates a fast, so it should invalidate ihram.
Their dalil relies on the presence of ejaculation as the trigger.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the illa for invalidation in hajj is actual intercourse, not ejaculation. Other acts are merely prohibited and require dam, not nullification.
The text states: 'Hajj is invalidated by intercourse; other prohibitions like wearing sewn clothes do not invalidate.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Contrast the practical outcomes: a Hanafi muhrim sacrifices a sheep and continues; a Shafi'i muhrim must sacrifice a camel and repeat the hajj.
This difference has significant implications for pilgrims.

امام شافعی نے احرام کو روز و پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی جس طرح مذکورہ چیزوں سے روزہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے بشرطیکہ انزال ہوا ہو اسی طرح ان چیزوں سے احترام بھی فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج ، جماع سے فاسد ہوتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جماع کے علاوہ دوسرے ممنوعات سے حج فاسد نہیں ہوتا۔ مثلا سلا ہوا کپڑا پہننے اور خوشبو وغیرہ کا استعمال کرنے سے حج فاسد نہیں ہوتا اور یہ مذکورہ چیزیں یعنی چھونا ، بوسہ لینا اور مادون الفرج میں جماع کرنا جماع مقصودی نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک طرح کا استلذاذ ہے۔ پس جب یہ چیزیں جماع نہیں تو ان کے ساتھ فساد حج بھی متعلق نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ جماع سے فساد حج متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ ان چیزوں میں عورت کے ساتھ لذت حاصل کرنے کے معنی موجود ہیں اور عورت کے ساتھ لذت حاصل کرنا احرام کے منوعات میں سے ہے اس لئے اس پر دم واجب ہو گا۔ برخلاف روزہ کے کیونکہ روزہ کے اندر شہوت پوری کرنا حرام ہے اور مادون الفرج میں بغیر انزال کے شہوت پوری کرنا حاصل نہیں ہوتا ۔ اس لئے بغیر انزال کے تو روزہ فاسد نہیں ہوگا البتہ اگر انزال ہو گیا تو روزہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔
The ruling of Allah is not attached to it as it is attached to intercourse. However, it contains the meaning of enjoyment and seeking pleasure with the woman, and this is prohibited. Therefore, a blood sacrifice becomes obligatory for it. Contrary to fasting, because in fasting, fulfilling desire is prohibited, and without ejaculation, this does not occur except through the private part. Explanation of the issue: If a muhrim looked with desire at the private part of his wife or another woman and ejaculated, then no blood sacrifice or other expiation is obligatory. Because in the state of ihram, intercourse is prohibited, and intercourse has not occurred, so nothing is obligatory. This is like if a muhrim sat thinking of a beautiful woman and ejaculated, nothing is obligatory. Similarly, looking at the private part also requires nothing. Intercourse is defined as the union of man and woman in form and the fulfillment of desire in meaning. The form of intercourse is that the man inserts his penis into the woman's vagina, and the meaning of intercourse is ejaculation. If a muhrim kissed a woman with desire or touched her, then a blood sacrifice is obligatory, whether he ejaculated or not. This is what is mentioned in al-Mabsut. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, ejaculation is a condition; thus it is stated that if he touched with desire and ejaculated, then a blood sacrifice is obligatory. From the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, it appears that if he did not ejaculate, then no blood sacrifice is obligatory on the muhrim. The author of al-Hidayah says: If a muhrim commits intercourse below the private part, i.e., on the thigh etc., then a blood sacrifice becomes obligatory, whether he ejaculated or not, as is the narration of al-Mabsut. It is narrated from Imam al-Shafi'i that in all these cases—i.e., kissing with desire, touching, and intercourse below the private part—if ejaculation occurs, then his ihram is invalidated. Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes ihram to fasting, meaning that just as the mentioned things invalidate fasting provided ejaculation occurs, similarly, these things invalidate ihram. Our proof is that hajj is invalidated by intercourse. This is the reason that hajj is not invalidated by other prohibitions except intercourse. For example, wearing sewn clothes and using perfume do not invalidate hajj. These mentioned things—touching, kissing, and intercourse below the private part—are not actual intercourse, but rather a kind of pleasure-seeking. So since these things are not intercourse, the invalidation of hajj is not attached to them, as it is attached to intercourse. However, it must be said that these things involve seeking pleasure with the woman, and seeking pleasure with a woman is among the prohibitions of ihram, so a blood sacrifice becomes obligatory. Contrary to fasting, because in fasting, fulfilling desire is prohibited, and without ejaculation, fulfilling desire below the private part does not occur. Therefore, without ejaculation, the fast is not invalidated, but if ejaculation occurs, then the fast is invalidated.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the rulings concerning a person in ihram (muhrim) who engages in acts of physical intimacy short of actual sexual intercourse. The passage first clarifies that looking at a woman's private part with desire, even if it leads to ejaculation, does not require any expiation (dam) because it does not constitute intercourse. The author defines intercourse as both the physical act (insertion) and the fulfillment of desire (ejaculation). Then it discusses kissing and touching with desire: according to al-Mabsut (a foundational Hanafi text), these acts require a dam regardless of ejaculation, while al-Jami' al-Saghir conditions it on ejaculation. The author of al-Hidayah prefers al-Mabsut's view, and adds that intercourse below the private part (e.g., between thighs) also requires dam. The passage then presents the Shafi'i objection: Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes ihram to fasting, arguing that just as these acts with ejaculation invalidate fasting, they should also invalidate ihram. The Hanafi response is that hajj is only invalidated by actual sexual intercourse (the real act of insertion). Other prohibited acts, like wearing sewn clothes or applying perfume, do not invalidate hajj; they only require expiation. Similarly, these intimate acts are not intercourse, so they do not invalidate ihram, but they do require dam because they involve seeking pleasure with a woman, which is prohibited in ihram. The comparison with fasting is rejected because fasting is invalidated by any act of fulfilling desire, which in the case of sub-private part contact only occurs with ejaculation, whereas in ihram, the prohibition is broader: any act of seeking pleasure is prohibited and requires compensation, but not invalidation. This distinction between the nature of prohibitions in hajj and fasting is key to understanding the Hanafi position. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that dam is obligatory for touching and kissing with desire, regardless of ejaculation, based on the Mabsut narration within Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
جماع (jimā‘): In this passage, jimā‘ refers to actual sexual intercourse involving insertion of the penis into the vagina, and also the fulfillment of desire through ejaculation.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as expiation for certain violations during ihram.
استلذاذ (istilzādh): Seeking or deriving pleasure, specifically sexual pleasure from a woman.
انزال (inzāl): Ejaculation of semen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the text, if a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) kisses his wife with desire and ejaculates, what is the ruling?
A) His hajj is invalidated and he must sacrifice a camel.
B) His hajj is valid but he must sacrifice a sheep (dam).
C) His hajj is invalidated and he must sacrifice a sheep.
D) Nothing is required; his hajj remains valid without any penalty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that only actual sexual intercourse invalidates hajj; other intimate acts with desire require a dam but do not nullify the pilgrimage.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Intercourse Before Arafat: The Hanafi Ruling and Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on expiation for intercourse before Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse before Arafat, explain the evidence for a sheep sacrifice, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using qiyas.

Core Idea
Intercourse before Arafat invalidates hajj, requires a sheep and qada'; Shafi'i analogy to post-Arafat intercourse is rebutted by hadith generality and qada' lightening the crime.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute in hajj rulings: what expiation is required if a muhrim has intercourse before standing at Arafat? The Hanafi school, relying on a specific hadith and the principle of qada', rules that a sheep suffices. Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes to intercourse after Arafat, requiring a camel. We'll break down the proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Intercourse before standing at Arafat. What is the Hanafi ruling? The hajj becomes fāsid (invalidated).
2
State the Hanafi expiation and qada'
The pilgrim must sacrifice a sheep (shāh) and perform a make-up hajj (qaḍā') the following year. These are wajib.
3
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is a hadith: the Prophet (ﷺ) said 'yuriqani dama' (they both pour out blood) and instructed the couple to continue their hajj and repeat it next year.
The hadith is general (muṭlaq) regarding the type of sacrifice.
4
Present the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shāfi'ī argues by qiyas: since intercourse after Arafat requires a camel (badanah), so too before Arafat should require a camel.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The hadith is general and cannot be restricted. (2) The obligation of qada' lightens the severity of the crime, so a sheep suffices. Additionally, note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether both passages invalidate hajj.

ترجمہ اور اگر محرم نے سبیلین میں سے کسی ایک میں وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے جماع کیا تو اس کا حج فاسد ہو جائے گا اور اس پر ایک بکری کی قربانی لازم ہوگی ۔ اور افعال حج اسی طرح کر گزرے جس طرح وہ شخص کر گذرتا ہے تو جنایت کے معنی خفیف ہو گئے اس لئے بکری پر اکتفاء کرے برخلاف وقوف کے بعد کے۔ کیونکہ (اس صورت میں) قضاء واجب نہیں ہے۔ پھر قدوری نے دونوں راہوں میں جماع یکساں قرار دیا۔ اور ابوحنیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ قبل کے علاوہ میں (یعنی مقعد میں ) وطی کرنا حج کو فاسد نہیں کرتا۔ کیونکہ ولی کے معنی ناقص ہو گئے ۔ پس ابوحنیفہ سے دو روایتیں ہوئیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے وقوف عرفہ سے پیشتر عورت کے قبل میں وہی کی یا مقعد میں کی تو عورت ومرد دونوں کا حج فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ اور ہر ایک پر بکری کی قربانی واجب ہے اور اونٹ، گائے وغیرہ میں ایک ایک حصہ واجب ہے۔ اور افعال حج اسی طرح پورے کرے جس طرح وہ شخص ادا کرتا ہے جس کا جرم خفیف ہو گیا۔ اور خفیف جرم میں بکری بھی کفایت کر جاتی ہے اس لئے بکری کی قربانی کافی ہے۔ اور حج کی قضاء اس لئے واجب کی گئی ہے تا کہ وہ حج جس کو شروع کیا تھا وہ درست ہو جائے ۔ اور وقف عرفہ کے بعد جماع کرنے کی صورت میں چونکہ حج فاسد نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے قضاء واجب نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے جرم خفیف نہیں ہوا بلکہ غلیظ ہی رہا اور جرم غلیظ میں بد نہ واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے وقوف عرفہ کے بعد جماع کرنے کی صورت میں بہد نہ واجب ہوگا بکری کفایت نہ کرے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام قدوری نے قبل اور ڈبر دونوں میں جماع کا حکم یکساں اور برابر قرار دیا ہے۔ یہی صاحبین کا مذہب ہے اور ایک روایت امام ابوحنیفہ کی ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے قبل کے اندر وہی کرنا تو مفسد حج
If he commits intercourse in one of the two passages before standing at Arafat, his hajj is invalidated and upon him is a sheep, and he continues in the hajj as one who did not invalidate it. The basis for this is what is narrated: that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) was asked about a man who had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram for hajj. He said: 'They both pour out blood (sacrifice), and they both continue in their hajj, and upon them is the hajj from next year.' And similarly it is transmitted from a group of the Companions. Al-Shafi'i said: A camel (badanah) is obligatory, by analogy with the case if he had intercourse after standing (at Arafat). The proof against him is the generality of what we narrated, and because when recompense (qada') became obligatory—and it is only obligatory for the sake of achieving the benefit—the nature of the crime became lightened, so a sheep suffices, unlike after standing because there is no recompense. Then (al-Quduri) made equal between the two passages. And from Abu Hanifa: that in other than the front passage (qiblah) it does not invalidate, due to the deficiency of the meaning of intercourse. So there are two narrations from him. Translation: And if the muhrim committed intercourse in one of the two passages before standing at Arafat, then his hajj is invalidated and upon him a sheep sacrifice is obligatory. And he should perform the acts of hajj just as a person who did not invalidate his hajj performs them. And the basis for this issue is the hadith that a man had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram for hajj, and the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered them to sacrifice a sheep (dam) and complete their hajj and perform it again the next year. It is similarly transmitted from a group of Companions. Imam al-Shafi'i said that a camel (badanah) is obligatory due to the gravity of the crime, by analogy with the case of intercourse after standing at Arafat. The proof against him is the generality of the hadith we narrated, and because when qada' (recompense) became obligatory—and it is only obligatory to achieve the benefit—the meaning of the crime became lightened, so a sheep suffices. Unlike after standing, because in that case qada' is not obligatory. Then al-Quduri made the ruling of intercourse in both passages equal. And from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that intercourse in other than the front passage (i.e., anal) does not invalidate hajj, because the meaning of intercourse is deficient. So there are two narrations from him. Explanation of the issue: If a muhrim performed intercourse in the front (vaginal) or back (anal) passage before standing at Arafat, then the hajj of both the man and woman is invalidated, and each must sacrifice a sheep, or they may share a part in a camel or cow. And he should complete the acts of hajj as one whose hajj is not invalidated, but he must make it up the following year. The basis of this issue is the hadith that a man had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram, and this occurred before standing at Arafat. The Prophet (ﷺ) ordered them both to sacrifice a sheep (dam) and said: 'Complete your hajj and perform qada' next year.' It is similarly transmitted from a group of the Companions. Imam al-Shafi'i said that due to this great crime, a camel (badanah) is obligatory, i.e., a camel or cow, and a sheep is not sufficient. He analogizes it to the case of intercourse after standing at Arafat, where a camel is obligatory. However, the hadith 'yuriqani dama' (they both pour out blood) is general, covering both sheep and camel; it should not be restricted to one without evidence. The second proof is that when qada' becomes obligatory due to the invalidation of hajj, the crime becomes lightened, and for a light crime a sheep suffices, so a sheep sacrifice is sufficient. Qada' of hajj is made obligatory so that the hajj which he began becomes correct. In the case of intercourse after standing at Arafat, since hajj is not invalidated, qada' is not obligatory, so the crime is not lightened but remains grave, and a grave crime requires a camel. Therefore, after standing at Arafat, a camel is obligatory and a sheep is not sufficient. The author of al-Hidayah says that al-Quduri made the ruling of intercourse in the front and back equal. This is the madhhab of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And there is one narration from Abu Hanifa. And from Abu Hanifa, a second narration is that intercourse in the front (vaginal) before standing at Arafat invalidates hajj (while anal does not).
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the ruling concerning a muhrim who has sexual intercourse before standing at Arafat. The core ruling is that such intercourse invalidates the hajj (makes it fāsid), and the pilgrim must continue the hajj rituals but also perform a qada' (make-up hajj) the following year. The required expiation (dam) is a sheep (shāh). The proof is a hadīth where the Prophet (ﷺ) instructed a couple who had intercourse while in ihrām to sacrifice a blood (dam), continue their hajj, and repeat it next year. This is also narrated from a group of Companions. Imam al-Shāfi'ī, however, argues that because intercourse after standing at 'Arafāt requires a camel (badanah), so too before 'Arafāt the sacrifice should be a camel, by analogy. The Hanafī response is twofold: First, the hadīth is general (mutlaq) in mentioning 'dam,' which includes a sheep; there is no justification to restrict it to a camel. Second, the obligation of qada' (making up the hajj) lightens the sin, so a sheep suffices. After 'Arafāt, no qada' is required (since hajj is not invalidated), so the sin remains grave and requires a camel. The passage also discusses an intra-Hanafī ikhtilāf: whether intercourse in the back passage (anal) invalidates hajj. According to the relied-upon view of al-Qudurī and the Sahibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad), both passages are equal; hajj is invalidated by either. But from Abū Hanīfa there are two narrations: one that both passages are equal (invalidating), and another that only vaginal intercourse invalidates hajj, because anal intercourse lacks the full meaning of wati' (sex). The passage ends mid-sentence with the second narration, but the ruling is clear: the muftā bihī is the view of the Sahibayn that both passages invalidate hajj before 'Arafāt, requiring a sheep sacrifice and qada'.

Key Terms
سبیلین (sabilayn): The two passages: the front passage (qiblah/vagina) and the back passage (dubur/anus).
شاۃ (shāh): A sheep or goat, the minimum expiation for certain violations in ihram.
بدنہ (badanah): A camel or cow used as a sacrificial animal in hajj.
قضاء (qaḍā’): The obligation to perform a make-up hajj the following year due to the invalidation of the current hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, what is the required sacrifice for a muhrim who has vaginal intercourse before standing at Arafat?
A) A camel (badanah)
B) A cow
C) A sheep (shāh)
D) Nothing; no sacrifice is required

Key Takeaway
Intercourse before Arafat invalidates hajj, requires a sheep and qada'; the Shafi'i analogue is rebutted by the general hadith and the principle of qada' lightening the sin.

Intercourse Before Wuquf: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof and cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse before Wuquf, identify the hadith proof, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Intercourse before Wuquf invalidates Hajj and requires a sheep — the obligation of qada lightens the sin.

This lesson examines a critical violation in Hajj: sexual intercourse before the standing at Arafah. The Hanafi school, relying on a prophetic hadith and the logic of qada, rules that the Hajj is invalidated but can be completed, and a sheep (dam) suffices as expiation. We will study the proof and contrast it with the Shafi'i position that requires a camel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what constitutes the violation (intercourse in either passage before Wuquf) and the Hanafi ruling: Hajj becomes invalid (fasid), a sheep is wajib, and qada (repeat next year) is required. The current Hajj must still be completed.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of the couple in ihram who had intercourse; the Prophet commanded them to sacrifice a sheep, complete their Hajj, and perform qada. This hadith is the primary proof (Sunnah ahad, zanni al-thubut).
The exact wording 'buraiqan dama' may be an OCR error.
3
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning for sheep
Because qada is obligatory to make up the lost benefit, the transgression (jinaya) is considered lighter. Hence, a sheep suffices. This contrasts with intercourse after Wuquf, where no qada is required, so a camel is necessary.
The reasoning: qada lightens the crime.
4
Review the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes to intercourse after Wuquf, where a camel is wajib, and argues the same should apply before Wuquf since both are major sins.
Qiyas after Wuquf → camel; before Wuquf → camel.
5
Examine the Hanafi response
The hadith is general (mutlaq) and includes both sheep and camel; there is no need to restrict it. Moreover, the presence of qada makes the sin lighter, so a sheep is appropriate. The Shafi'i qiyas is overridden by the explicit hadith.
Al-amm yufidu al-wujub but not restricted unless proven.

Considering it analogously to what if he had intercourse after Wuquf. And the proof against him is the general application of what we narrated, and because when qada became obligatory, and it is not obligatory except for the purpose of seeking the benefit, the meaning of transgression becomes light, so a sheep suffices, unlike after Wuquf because there is no qada. Then he equated between the two passages. And from Abu Hanifa that in other than the front (i.e., the back) it does not corrupt it due to the deficient meaning of intercourse, so there are two narrations from him. Translation: And if a muhrim has intercourse in one of the two passages before Wuquf at Arafah, then his Hajj becomes invalid, and a sacrificial sheep becomes obligatory upon him. And he should perform the acts of Hajj in the same way as a person whose Hajj is not invalidated does. The basis of this issue is the hadith that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was asked about a person who had intercourse with his wife while both were in the sanctity of Hajj, so he said: Both should offer one sacrifice, both should complete their Hajj, and both are obligated to perform Hajj the following year. Similarly, it is narrated from a group of the Companions. Imam Shafi'i said that a camel is obligatory by analogy with the case of intercourse after Wuquf. The proof against Imam Shafi'i is the general application of this hadith which we have narrated, and because when qada became obligatory, and qada is not obligatory except for achieving the benefit, the meaning of transgression becomes light, so a sheep suffices, unlike after Wuquf because in that case qada is not obligatory. Then Quduri equated intercourse in both passages. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that intercourse in other than the front (i.e., the anus) does not invalidate Hajj because the meaning of intercourse is deficient. So there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. Commentary: If a muhrim has intercourse in the front or back of a woman before Wuquf, then the Hajj of both the man and woman becomes invalid. And each must sacrifice a sheep, or a share in a camel or cow. And they should complete the acts of Hajj as a person whose Hajj is not invalid does. However, they must make it up the following year. The basis of this issue is the hadith that a man had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram, and this occurred before Wuquf, so the Prophet commanded both to offer a dam, i.e., a sheep, and said: Complete the acts of Hajj and make it up next year. It is also narrated similarly from a group of Companions. Imam Shafi'i says that due to this great sin, a badanah (camel or cow) is obligatory, a sheep is insufficient. He analogizes to the case of intercourse after Wuquf where a badanah is required. But the hadith 'buraiqan dama' is general, including both sheep and camel, and should not be restricted arbitrarily. The second proof is that when qada became obligatory due to the invalidation of Hajj, the crime became light, and a sheep suffices for a light crime. The qada of Hajj is obligated so that the Hajj he started becomes correct. In the case of intercourse after Wuquf, since the Hajj is not invalidated and qada is not obligated, the crime remains severe, and a severe crime requires a badanah. The author of Hidayah says that Imam Quduri equated the ruling of intercourse in the front and back. This is the madhhab of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). There is one narration from Abu Hanifa, and another narration from Abu Hanifa that intercourse in the front before Wuquf invalidates Hajj, but intercourse in the back does not, because complete intercourse occurs in the front, while in the back it is deficient. So regarding intercourse in the back, there are two narrations: one of invalidation and one of non-invalidation.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with an inter-madhhab element. It addresses the ruling on sexual intercourse before Wuquf in Hajj. The main Hanafi position (from the Sahibayn) is that intercourse in either the front or back passage before Wuquf invalidates Hajj for both spouses and requires a sheep (shah) as expiation, along with completing the current Hajj and making it up the next year. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet commanded a couple in a similar situation to sacrifice a sheep. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that a camel is required by analogy with intercourse after Wuquf. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the hadith is general and includes a sheep, so no restriction; (2) the obligation of qada lightens the crime, making a sheep sufficient. The passage then highlights an internal Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa has two narrations on whether intercourse in the back (dubr) invalidates the Hajj. One narration follows the Sahibayn (both passages corrupt), another holds that only the front corrupts because the act is considered incomplete. The relied-upon position in the Hidayah (via Quduri) is the Sahibayn's view that both passages are equal. The reasoning: the meaning of transgression is lighter when qada is required, so a sheep suffices; after Wuquf, no qada is needed, so the crime is severe and a camel is due.

Key Terms
سبیلین (sabīlayn): The two passages: the front (vagina) and the back (anus).
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal, specifically a sheep or goat, offered as expiation (jaza').
قضاء (qaḍā'): The compensatory performance of a corrupted Hajj in a subsequent year.
بدنہ (badanah): A sacrificial camel (or cow) offered as expiation.

D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that intercourse before Wuquf invalidates Hajj, but the obligation of qada lightens the expiation to a sheep, not a camel.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Are Both Passages Equal?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the equal status of the two passages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding intercourse in the back passage before Wuquf and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn rule both passages equal; Abu Hanifa has two narrations—the madhhab relies on equality.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a subtle disagreement on whether intercourse in the back passage (dubr) before Wuquf invalidates Hajj in the same way as vaginal intercourse. This lesson examines the views of the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa, and the tarjih that settles the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the view of the Sahibayn
Imam Quduri equated the two passages; this is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: both vaginal and anal intercourse before Wuquf invalidate Hajj equally.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's two narrations
From Abu Hanifa, there are two narrations: (1) same as the Sahibayn (equality), and (2) only vaginal intercourse invalidates; anal intercourse does not because it is deficient.
The second narration considers the act incomplete (naqis).
3
Understand the reasoning for the limiting narration
The limiting narration argues that complete intercourse (wat' kamil) only occurs in the front (qibl). Anal intercourse is deficient, so it does not cause the same nullification.
'Taqasur ma'na al-wat'i' – deficiency in the meaning of intercourse.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the madhhab is that of the Sahibayn: both passages are equal. This is the view adopted by Quduri and followed in the Hidayah.
Tarjih: the Sahibayn's view is preferred.
5
Note the practical consequence
In practice, a muhrim who engages in anal intercourse before Wuquf must treat his Hajj as invalid, complete it, offer a sheep, and perform qada the next year, just as with vaginal intercourse.
The difference only affects academic discussion of the riwayahs, not the operative fatwa.

Considering it analogously to what if he had intercourse after Wuquf. And the proof against him is the general application of what we narrated, and because when qada became obligatory, and it is not obligatory except for the purpose of seeking the benefit, the meaning of transgression becomes light, so a sheep suffices, unlike after Wuquf because there is no qada. Then he equated between the two passages. And from Abu Hanifa that in other than the front (i.e., the back) it does not corrupt it due to the deficient meaning of intercourse, so there are two narrations from him. Translation: And if a muhrim has intercourse in one of the two passages before Wuquf at Arafah, then his Hajj becomes invalid, and a sacrificial sheep becomes obligatory upon him. And he should perform the acts of Hajj in the same way as a person whose Hajj is not invalidated does. The basis of this issue is the hadith that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was asked about a person who had intercourse with his wife while both were in the sanctity of Hajj, so he said: Both should offer one sacrifice, both should complete their Hajj, and both are obligated to perform Hajj the following year. Similarly, it is narrated from a group of the Companions. Imam Shafi'i said that a camel is obligatory by analogy with the case of intercourse after Wuquf. The proof against Imam Shafi'i is the general application of this hadith which we have narrated, and because when qada became obligatory, and qada is not obligatory except for achieving the benefit, the meaning of transgression becomes light, so a sheep suffices, unlike after Wuquf because in that case qada is not obligatory. Then Quduri equated intercourse in both passages. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that intercourse in other than the front (i.e., the anus) does not invalidate Hajj because the meaning of intercourse is deficient. So there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. Commentary: If a muhrim has intercourse in the front or back of a woman before Wuquf, then the Hajj of both the man and woman becomes invalid. And each must sacrifice a sheep, or a share in a camel or cow. And they should complete the acts of Hajj as a person whose Hajj is not invalid does. However, they must make it up the following year. The basis of this issue is the hadith that a man had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram, and this occurred before Wuquf, so the Prophet commanded both to offer a dam, i.e., a sheep, and said: Complete the acts of Hajj and make it up next year. It is also narrated similarly from a group of Companions. Imam Shafi'i says that due to this great sin, a badanah (camel or cow) is obligatory, a sheep is insufficient. He analogizes to the case of intercourse after Wuquf where a badanah is required. But the hadith 'buraiqan dama' is general, including both sheep and camel, and should not be restricted arbitrarily. The second proof is that when qada became obligatory due to the invalidation of Hajj, the crime became light, and a sheep suffices for a light crime. The qada of Hajj is obligated so that the Hajj he started becomes correct. In the case of intercourse after Wuquf, since the Hajj is not invalidated and qada is not obligated, the crime remains severe, and a severe crime requires a badanah. The author of Hidayah says that Imam Quduri equated the ruling of intercourse in the front and back. This is the madhhab of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). There is one narration from Abu Hanifa, and another narration from Abu Hanifa that intercourse in the front before Wuquf invalidates Hajj, but intercourse in the back does not, because complete intercourse occurs in the front, while in the back it is deficient. So regarding intercourse in the back, there are two narrations: one of invalidation and one of non-invalidation.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with an inter-madhhab element. It addresses the ruling on sexual intercourse before Wuquf in Hajj. The main Hanafi position (from the Sahibayn) is that intercourse in either the front or back passage before Wuquf invalidates Hajj for both spouses and requires a sheep (shah) as expiation, along with completing the current Hajj and making it up the next year. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet commanded a couple in a similar situation to sacrifice a sheep. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that a camel is required by analogy with intercourse after Wuquf. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) the hadith is general and includes a sheep, so no restriction; (2) the obligation of qada lightens the crime, making a sheep sufficient. The passage then highlights an internal Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa has two narrations on whether intercourse in the back (dubr) invalidates the Hajj. One narration follows the Sahibayn (both passages corrupt), another holds that only the front corrupts because the act is considered incomplete. The relied-upon position in the Hidayah (via Quduri) is the Sahibayn's view that both passages are equal. The reasoning: the meaning of transgression is lighter when qada is required, so a sheep suffices; after Wuquf, no qada is needed, so the crime is severe and a camel is due.

Key Terms
سبیلین (sabīlayn): The two passages: the front (vagina) and the back (anus).
رِوَايَتَان (riwāyatān): Two narrations (from Imam Abu Hanifa) on the same issue.
وَطْء كامل (waṭ' kāmil): Complete intercourse, which in Hanafi terminology is vaginal penetration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view in the Hanafi school regarding intercourse in the back passage before Wuquf?
A) It does not invalidate Hajj.
B) It invalidates Hajj equally to vaginal intercourse.
C) It requires a camel instead of a sheep.
D) It requires no expiation.

Key Takeaway
Although Abu Hanifa has two narrations, the Hanafi school relies on the Sahibayn's view that both passages equally invalidate Hajj before Wuquf.

Spousal Separation During Qada of Corrupted Hajj: Hanafi View
Hanafi ruling on whether spouses must separate during qada Hajj, with opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on spousal separation during qada Hajj, explain the opposing views, and evaluate the Hanafi argument.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, the marriage bond and the deterrent of hardship make spousal separation unnecessary during qada Hajj.

This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a delicate fiqh issue: when a husband and wife have corrupted their Hajj by intercourse before Wuquf, must they separate when they perform the qada (makeup) Hajj in a later year? The Hanafi school holds that separation is not required, while Malik, Zufar (a Hanafi scholar), and Shafi'i require separation at different points. The debate turns on whether the marriage bond or the risk of repeated sin should determine the ruling. Through this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi reasoning and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: according to the Hanafi school, spouses are not obligated to separate during the qada of a corrupted Hajj or Umrah. The ruling is mubah (permissible to stay together), not wajib.
The text states 'indana' (according to us) to mark the Hanafi position.
2
Identify the opposing views
Three different positions are mentioned: Malik says separate upon leaving home; Zufar says upon entering ihram; Shafi'i says upon reaching the location of the original sin.
Imam Ahmad holds a similar view to Shafi'i.
3
Analyze the opponents' proof
The opponents rely on a saying of the Companions: 'When they return for qada, they separate.' They also argue that remembering the previous sin could lead to recurrence, so preventive separation is necessary.
The text cites the saying and each imam interprets the timing differently.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is based on two points: (1) the marriage bond (nikah) remains intact, so separation before ihram is meaningless because intercourse is permissible; (2) after ihram, the memory of the severe hardship suffered due to a temporary pleasure will deter them from repeating the sin, making forced separation unnecessary.
The Hanafi school prioritizes the bond of marriage and psychological deterrence over a rule of strict separation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, the couple can travel together, share accommodation, and perform the rituals side by side. In the other schools, they must take different routes or physically separate at various stages, potentially causing hardship and marital strain.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is no separation, and Zufar's contrary view is not relied upon.

مالک کا اختلاف ہے ب وہ دونوں اپنے گھر سے نکلیں۔ اور امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے جب وہ دونوں احرام باندھیں ۔ اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے جب وہ دونوں اس مکان پر پہنچیں جہاں اس نے بیوی کے ساتھ جماع کیا تھا۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد و عورت دونوں گذشتہ واقعہ کو یاد کریں گے تو مجامعت میں پڑ جائیں گے۔ اس لئے دونوں جدار ہیں۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد و عورت دونوں کو یکجا کرنے والا اور وہ دونوں میں نکاح برابر موجود ہے۔ تو احرام سے پہلے جدائی کے کوئی معنی نہیں کیونکہ ابھی جماع مباح ہے۔ اور نہ احرام کے بعد کیونکہ وہ دونوں اس مشقت شدیدہ کو یاد کریں گے جو ان دونوں کو لاحق ہوئی معمولی سی لذت کی وجہ سے۔ پس دونوں کی ندامت اور پر ہیز گاری میں اضافہ ہی ہو گا اس لئے جدائی کے کچھ معنی نہیں ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جماع کی وجہ سے فاسد کردہ حج یا عمرہ کی جب قضا کریں تو مرد و عورت پر جدار ہنا ہمارے نزدیک واجب نہیں ہے یعنی یہ واجب نہیں ہے کہ دونوں دور استے اختیار کریں۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا ہے کہ گھر سے نکلتے ہی دونوں جدا ہو جائیں اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب احرام باندھ لیں تو جدا ہو جائیں۔ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ سال گذشتہ جس جگہ جماع کیا تھا جب اسکے قریب آئیں تو جدائی اختیار کر لیں ۔ یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضا کے سفر میں مرد و عورت جب گذشتہ واقعہ کو یاد کریں گے تو وہ جماع میں مبتلا ہو جائیں گے اس لئے دونوں الگ الگ سفر کریں۔ صاحب عنایہ نے کہا کہ اصل اس مسئلہ میں صحابہ کا یہ قول ہے إِذَا رَجَعَا لِلْقَضَاءِ يَفْتَرِقَانِ ۔ یعنی جب دونوں قضاء کے لئے لوٹیں تو جدا جدا ہو جائیں یعنی ایک کا راستہ دوسرے کے راستہ سے مختلف ہو۔ پس امام مالک نے ظاہر لفظ کو اختیار کیا اور فرمایا کہ گھر سے نکلتے ہی جدا ہونا واجب ہے۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ وقت احترام سے جدا ہونا ضروی ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جب اس مکان کے قریب تر ہو جائیں جہاں جماع کیا تھا تو جدا ہو جائیں۔ کیونکہ اس جگہ پہنچ کر جب سابقہ جماع کو یاد کریں گے تو ان کی شہوت برانگیختہ کرے گی اور جماع میں مبتلا ہوں گے اس لئے اس سے پہلے ہی جدائی اختیار کرلیں ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں کو یکجا جمع کرنے والا نکاح ہے اور وہ ابھی قائم ہے۔ پس نہ تو احرام باندھنے سے پہلے جدائی کے
Is it necessary to separate the wife during the qada of Hajj? Statements of jurists. And according to us, it is not obligatory for him to separate from his wife in the qada of what they corrupted, contrary to Malik when they leave their home, and to Zufar when they enter ihram, and to al-Shafi'i when they reach the place where he had intercourse with her. Their proof is that they will remember that and fall into intercourse, so they separate. Our proof is that the bond between them, which is marriage, remains intact, so there is no meaning to separation before ihram because intercourse is permissible, nor after ihram because they will remember the severe hardship that befell them due to a small pleasure, so they will be filled with regret and caution, so there is no meaning to separation. Translation: And according to us, it is not obligatory for a muhrim to separate from his wife in the qada of a corrupted Hajj or Umrah. Imam Malik holds that they should separate when they leave their home. Imam Zufar holds that they should separate when they enter ihram. Imam Shafi'i holds that they should separate when they reach the place where he had intercourse with her. Their proof is that the man and woman will remember the past incident and fall into intercourse, so they should separate. Our proof is that the one who brings them together is marriage and that remains intact. So separation before ihram has no meaning because intercourse is then permissible, nor after ihram because they will remember the severe hardship that befell them due to a trivial pleasure, so they will increase in regret and piety. Therefore, separation has no meaning. Commentary: The issue is that when making qada of a Hajj or Umrah corrupted by intercourse, according to us it is not obligatory for the spouses to separate. Malik said they separate as soon as they leave the house; Zufar said they separate upon ihram; Shafi'i said they separate when they approach the place where the intercourse occurred last year. The author of Hidayah states their proof: during the journey of qada, if they remember the past incident, they may fall into intercourse, so they should travel separately. The author of Inayah said the basis of this issue is the saying of the Companions: 'When they return for qada, they separate.' Malik took the apparent meaning and said separation is wajib upon leaving the house; Zufar said upon ihram; Shafi'i said when they approach the place of intercourse. Our proof is that they are brought together by marriage which remains intact. So before ihram there is no separation because intercourse is permissible, and after ihram they will remember the hardship and be deterred.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether spouses who corrupted their Hajj by intercourse must separate during the qada (makeup) Hajj. The Hanafi position is clear: separation is not obligatory. The reason is that the marriage bond (nikah) remains valid and intact. Before ihram, intercourse is permissible anyway, so separation has no purpose. After ihram, they are reminded of the severe hardship they endured due to their sin, which will make them regretful and cautious, preventing them from repeating the act. Therefore, forced separation is unnecessary. The opponents—Malik, Zufar (a Hanafi scholar), and Shafi'i—argue that separation prevents recurrence of sin. Malik says separate from the start of the journey; Zufar says upon ihram; Shafi'i says at the location of the previous intercourse. They rely on a saying of the Companions: 'When they return for qada, they separate.' The Hanafi response refutes this by emphasizing that the nikah bond negates the need for separation, and the memory of hardship acts as a deterrent. The commentary adds that Imam Ahmad held the same view as Shafi'i. The passage reinforces that the Hanafi school prioritizes the existing marital relationship and the psychological deterrent over preventive separation.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): The compensatory performance of a corrupted Hajj or Umrah in a later year.
افتراق (iftirāq): Separation of spouses during travel, meaning they take different routes or travel separately.
بدنہ (badanah): A camel or cow (large sacrificial animal), mentioned in the previous lesson as required by Shafi'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it not obligatory for spouses to separate during the qada of a corrupted Hajj?
A) Because the qada is not wajib
B) Because marriage bond remains and the hardship deters them
C) Because they have already repented
D) Because they are not in ihram anymore

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, spousal separation during qada Hajj is not required because the marriage bond and the deterrent of hardship outweigh the need for preventive separation.
