Separation of Spouses During Qada of Corrupted Hajj: Hanafi vs Others
Dispute among Hanafi, Maliki, Zufar, and Shafi'i on separation requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on spousal separation during qada of corrupted Hajj and evaluate the opposing arguments of Malik, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Marriage remains intact; hardship deters repetition — Hanafi: no separation required.

This passage from al-Hidayah tackles a practical dilemma: when a couple's Hajj is corrupted by intercourse, must they separate during the make-up journey? The Hanafi school says no, while Malik, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i each require separation at different stages. Their reasoning and the Hanafi response reveal how legal principles (here the strength of the marriage contract and human psychology) shape divergent rulings. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh competing masalih.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: separation is not wajib; it is only mandub if fitnah is feared. Note the explicit phrase 'laysa 'alayhi an yufāriqa' from the matn.
This is the statement of the text (al-Hidayah) and represents Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing views
List the three opponents: Malik (separation from home), Zufar (at ihram), al-Shafi'i (at the spot of intercourse). Also note that Ahmad follows al-Shafi'i.
The variation in timing shows different assessments of when temptation peaks.
3
Follow the opponents' proof
Extract their dalil: being together will remind them of the past sin and lead to repetition. Therefore, to prevent sin, they must be separated beforehand.
This is a preventive (sadd al-dhara'i') reasoning.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the two-part rebuttal: (a) before ihram, intercourse is still permissible, so separation is pointless; (b) after ihram, the memory of the severe hardship endured due to a minor pleasure will deter them more than any temptation.
The Hanafi argument uses a rational (aqli) proof based on marriage continuity and psychological deterrent.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: Hanafi couples travel together; others must separate at various points. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position, and separation is only recommended when fitnah is feared.
The companion saying 'ifāda lil-qadā' yaftariqān' is interpreted as mandub, not wajib.

وَ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُفَارِقَ امْرَأَتَهُ فِي قَضَاءِ مَا أَفْسَدَاهُ عِندَنَا خِلَاقًا لِمَالِكَ إِذَا خَرَجَا مِنْ بَيْتِهِمَا وَلِزَفُر إِذَا أَحْرَمَا وَلِلشَّافِعِي إِذَا انْتَهَيَا إِلَى الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي جَامَعَهَا فِيْهِ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ مَا يَتَذَا كَرَانِ ذَلِكَ فَيَفَعَانِ فِي الْمَوَاقِعَةِ فَيَفْتَرِقَانِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الجَامِعَ وَهُوَ النِّكَاحُ بَيْنَهُمَا قَائِمَ فَلَا مَعْنَى الْإِفْتِرَاقِ قَبلَ الْإِحْرَامِ لَا بَاحَةِ الْوِقَاعِ وَلَا بَعْدَهُ يَتَذَاكَرَانِ مَالَحِقَهُمَا مِنَ الْمُشَقَّةِ الشَّدِيدَةِ بِسَبَبٍ لَذَّةٍ يَسِيرَةٍ فَيْرُ دَا دَانِ نَدْمًا وَ تَحَرُّزًا فَلَا مَعْنَى لِلْافْتَرَاقِ
ترجمہ اور ہمارے نزدیک محرم پر واجب نہیں کہ وہ اپنی بیوی کو فاسد کردہ حج یا عمرہ کی قضاء میں جدا کرے امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے ب وہ دونوں اپنے گھر سے نکلیں۔ اور امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے جب وہ دونوں احرام احمد کا قول ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضا کے سفر میں مرد و عورت جب گذشتہ واقعہ کو یاد کریں گے تو وہ جماع میں مبتلا ہو جائیں گے اس لئے دونوں الگ الگ سفر کریں۔ صاحب عنایہ نے ظاہر لفظ کو اختیار کیا اور فرمایا کہ گھر سے نکلتے ہی جدا ہونا واجب ہے۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ وقت احترام سے جدا ہونا ضروی ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جب اس مکان کے قریب تر ہو جائیں جہاں جماع کیا تھا تو جدا ہو جائیں۔ کیونکہ اس جگہ پہنچ کر جب سابقہ جماع کو یاد کریں گے تو ان کی شہوت برانگیختہ کرے گی اور جماع میں مبتلا ہوں گے اس لئے اس سے پہلے ہی جدائی اختیار کرلیں ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں کو یکجا جمع کرنے والا نکاح ہے اور وہ ابھی قائم ہے۔ پس نہ تو احرام باندھنے سے پہلے جدائی کے کوئی معنی اور نہ احرام کے بعد ۔ احرام سے پہلے تو اس لئے کہ احرام سے پہلے جماع کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور احرام کے بعد اس لئے کہ ان کو ہر آن یہ بات یاد آتی رہے گی کہ یہ دوسرے سفر کی مشقت معمولی سی لذت کی وجہ سے اٹھانی پڑ رہی ہے پس یہ دونوں اس کو یاد کر کے نادم بھی ہوں گے اور پر ہیز کی کوشش بھی کریں گے۔ اس لئے دونوں کو جدا کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہے۔ اور رہا صحابہ کا قول تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دونوں کا جدا ہونا مندوب ہے اگر فتنہ میں پڑ جانے کا اندیشہ ہو۔
He is not obligated to separate from his wife in the qada of what they corrupted, according to us, contrary to Malik when they leave their house, and to Zufar when they enter ihram, and to al-Shafi'i when they reach the place where he had intercourse with her. Their proof is that they will remember that and will fall into intercourse, so they should separate. Our proof is that the uniting factor, which is marriage, exists between them, so there is no meaning to separation before ihram because intercourse is permissible, nor after ihram because they will remember the severe hardship that befell them due to a minor pleasure, so they will be deterred with regret and caution, thus no meaning to separation. (Urdu commentary:) And according to us, it is not obligatory for the muhrim to separate from his wife in the qada of a corrupted Hajj or Umrah. Imam Malik differs: when they both leave their house. Imam Zufar differs: when they both enter ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i differs: when they both reach the place where he had intercourse with her. Their proof: the man and woman will remember the past event and will fall into intercourse, so they should separate. Our proof: the one that unites them, i.e., marriage, remains present. Therefore, separation before ihram has no meaning because intercourse is still permissible. Nor after ihram because they will remember the severe hardship that befell them due to a minor pleasure; so their regret and caution will increase; therefore separation has no meaning. Explanation: The issue is that when performing qada of a Hajj or Umrah corrupted by intercourse, it is not obligatory for the man and woman to separate, according to us. Imam Malik said they should separate as soon as they leave the house. Imam Zufar said when they enter ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i said when they approach the place where intercourse occurred. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. According to the author of al-Hidayah, their proof is that in the journey of qada, when the man and woman remember the past event, they will fall into intercourse, so they should travel separately. The author of al-'Inayah said that the basis of this issue is the statement of the Companions: 'When they return for qada, they should separate.' That is, when both return for qada, they should separate, meaning each takes a different route. Imam Malik took the apparent wording and said separation is obligatory upon leaving the house. Imam Zufar said separation is necessary at the time of ihram. Imam al-Shafi'i said when they come close to the place where intercourse occurred, they should separate, because upon reaching that place, when they remember the previous intercourse, their desire will be aroused and they will fall into intercourse, so they should separate beforehand. Our proof is that the one uniting them is marriage, which still exists. So neither before ihram nor after ihram is there any meaning to separation. Before ihram because intercourse is permissible before ihram, and after ihram because they will constantly remember that they are enduring the hardship of a second journey due to a minor pleasure; thus they will regret and strive to avoid it. Therefore, there is no meaning in separating them. As for the saying of the Companions, the answer is that their separation is recommended (mandub) if there is fear of falling into fitnah.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a husband and wife must separate during the qada (make-up) of a Hajj or Umrah that was corrupted by sexual intercourse. The Hanafi position, attributed to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, is that separation is not obligatory. The text notes three opposing views: Imam Malik requires separation from the moment they leave their home; Imam Zufar requires separation at the time of entering ihram; and Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) require separation when they reach the specific place where the original intercourse occurred. The opponents' rationale is that being together will lead them to remember the past sin and possibly repeat it. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, before ihram, intercourse is still permissible, so separation has no purpose; second, after ihram, the memory of the severe hardship endured due to a minor pleasure will actually reinforce their regret and caution, thus deterring them from repeating the act. The author also addresses the companion saying 'when they return for qada, they should separate', explaining that this indicates recommendation, not obligation, if there is fear of fitnah.

Key Terms
قَضَاء (qadā'): The make-up or compensation of a corrupted or missed religious obligation, here Hajj/Umrah.
إِفْسَاد (ifsād): The act of corrupting a valid Hajj/Umrah, typically by sexual intercourse before the tahlil point.
فِرَاق (firāq): Separation or disunion between spouses during the qada journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is separation not required during the qada of a corrupted Hajj?
A) Because the marriage is still valid and the hardship will deter them
B) Because the Hajj is already invalid
C) Because the couple must stay together for safety
D) Because the wife is not required to perform Hajj

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, separation during qada of corrupted Hajj is not obligatory; the marriage remains and the hardship of the journey deters repetition.
